### Beyond Borders Gazette (@bb_gazette)
_Fri Jun 05 17:20:06 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/bb_gazette/status/2062947584742920575)

> Researchers at Monash University have developed a tiny chip that could help pave the way for computers that process information using light instead of electricity. Published in the journal Nature Photonics, the study demonstrates a nanoscale device capable of generating, controlling and reading light-based signals on a single platform. The breakthrough uses an emerging technology called valleytronics, which relies on quantum properties in advanced materials to encode information. Researchers say the innovation could lead to faster computing, lower energy consumption and more efficient communication systems in the future.
>
> Investigadores de la Universidad Monash desarrollaron un diminuto chip que podría ayudar a abrir el camino hacia computadoras capaces de procesar información utilizando luz en lugar de electricidad. Publicado en la revista Nature Photonics, el estudio demuestra un dispositivo a escala nanométrica capaz de generar, controlar y leer señales basadas en luz en una sola plataforma. El avance utiliza una tecnología emergente conocida como valleytrónica, que aprovecha propiedades cuánticas de materiales avanzados para codificar información. Los investigadores afirman que la innovación podría conducir a una computación más rápida, un menor consumo de energía y sistemas de comunicación más eficientes en el futuro.
>
> #Chip #Information #Light #TechInvestigation #valleytronics

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKEP5I_bEAA66WO.jpg

### SailorSBG (@NucSBG)
_Fri Jun 05 17:20:55 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/NucSBG/status/2062947792008413666)

> ============================================================
> SOLIDIFICATION OF LIGHT AND PROGRAMMABLE MATTER
> Connection Brief
> ============================================================
>
> Solidification of Light:
> - Refers to experiments making photons behave like condensed matter.
> - Key breakthrough (March 2025): Italian researchers created the first
>   "photonic supersolid" — light that has a rigid crystalline structure
>   (solid-like) while flowing without friction (superfluid-like).
> - Achieved using exciton-polaritons in semiconductor nanostructures.
>
> Programmable Matter:
> - Materials that can change physical properties (shape, density,
>   optical traits, stiffness) in a controlled/programmable way.
> - Includes metamaterials, shape-changing systems, and modular robotics.
>
> Connections:
> 1. Light as a programmable medium: Supersolid light and polariton
>    systems allow dynamic, reconfigurable quantum states controlled
>    by lasers or external fields.
>
> 2. Programmable photonics overlap: Solid-light phenomena can serve
>    as building blocks for adaptive optical chips, tunable lasers,
>    optical neural networks, and quantum simulators.
>
> 3. Hybrid future tech: Combines exotic quantum behavior of "solid"
>    light with the reconfigurability of smart materials, enabling
>    potential applications in quantum computing, adaptive optics,
>    and light-based programmable devices.
>
> Current status: Mostly laboratory-scale quantum experiments, but
> strong conceptual bridge toward future smart photonic materials.
>
> References:
> [1] Live Science / Nature (2025) - Photonic supersolid creation
> [2] Wikipedia / ScienceAlert - Solid light and supersolids
> [3] Wikipedia - Programmable matter
> [4] Related works on polaritons and programmable photonics

### Piggo’s Trading Desk (@Piggos_T_Desk)
_Fri Jun 05 17:23:44 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 4 · ↻ 2 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/Piggos_T_Desk/status/2062948497977196803)

> 🚨 Photonics may become the most important technology shift of the next decade.
>
> Not AI software.
>
> Not apps.
>
> Not even GPUs alone.
>
> The REAL revolution may be the replacement of electricity with LIGHT inside computing infrastructure. 🧵
>
> Silicon electronics are approaching physical limits.
>
> Modern AI infrastructure now faces: ⚠️ bandwidth ceilings ⚠️ power-consumption explosions ⚠️ heat-density problems ⚠️ latency bottlenecks ⚠️ interconnect saturation
>
> The current architecture is becoming unsustainable.
>
> This is where photonics enters.
>
> Photonics = using LIGHT (photons) instead of electricity (electrons) to: 💡 transmit data 💡 process signals 💡 move information 💡 scale compute infrastructure
>
> The implications are enormous.
>
> We believe photonics is no longer speculative science fiction.
>
> It is increasingly becoming: ⚠️ necessary ⚠️ commercially viable ⚠️ strategically essential
>
> Especially for hyperscale AI systems.
>
> The AI boom itself is creating the problem photonics solves.
>
> As models scale: 📈 compute demand explodes 📈 rack density rises 📈 cooling loads surge 📈 electricity consumption skyrockets
>
> Copper interconnects increasingly become the bottleneck.
>
> Traditional electrical systems waste massive amounts of energy as heat.
>
> Photonics changes the equation: ⚡ lower power consumption ⚡ faster transmission ⚡ lower latency ⚡ higher bandwidth ⚡ less thermal stress
>
> This is why hyperscalers are aggressively pursuing it.
>
> In this case the sequence is straightforward:
>
> Step 1: 🤖 AI models scale exponentially
>
> Step 2: ⚠️ Electrical interconnects hit limits
>
> Step 3: 🔥 Cooling and power costs explode
>
> Step 4: 💡 Photonics becomes economically necessary
>
> Step 5: 🏗 Entire data-center architecture changes
>
> This transition is already happening quietly.
>
> Over the next 3–5 years: ⚠️ co-packaged optics ⚠️ optical switching ⚠️ silicon photonics ⚠️ photonic networking
>
> …will increasingly replace traditional copper infrastructure.
>
> The implications go far beyond performance.
>
> Photonics may fundamentally reshape: 🏭 semiconductor design ⚡ power consumption 💧 cooling infrastructure 🧠 AI deployment economics 🏢 hyperscale construction
>
> We believe this becomes one of the clearest examples of K-shaped technological consolidation.
>
> Why?
>
> Because only the largest players can afford: 💰 photonic R&D 💰 custom AI infrastructure 💰 advanced packaging 💰 optical integration (Watch chip makers rotating, new partnerships)
>
> Smaller competitors increasingly get locked out.
>
> The photonics transition favors: ✅ hyperscalers ✅ mega-cap semiconductor firms ✅ defense-linked infrastructure players ✅ vertically integrated ecosystems
>
> The technological moat widens.
>
> 🚨 INVESTABLE PLAYERS
>
> Several companies already sit directly inside this transition.
>
> ⚡ Broadcom ($AVGO) ⚡ Coherent ($COHR) ⚡ Lumentum ($LITE) ⚡ Intel ($INTC) ⚡ Laser Photonics ($LASE)
>
> Each attacks a different layer of the stack.
>
> $AVGO is one of the strongest large-cap photonics plays.
>
> Broadcom already dominates: 🔌 networking 🔌 optical connectivity 🔌 silicon-photonics infrastructure 🔌 AI data-center interconnects
>
> It sits directly at the AI bandwidth bottleneck.
>
> $COHR is another critical player.
>
> Coherent controls: 💡 industrial lasers 💡 optical subsystems 💡 photonic components 💡 semiconductor manufacturing optics
>
> As photonic infrastructure scales, laser demand scales with it.
>
> $LITE remains deeply leveraged to: 📡 fiber optics 📡 telecom photonics 📡 optical sensing 📡 AI networking expansion
>
> The company effectively monetizes bandwidth growth itself.
>
> $INTC is quietly positioning aggressively in silicon photonics.
>
> Intel understands a critical reality:
>
> Traditional scaling alone is no longer enough.
>
> Future compute increasingly depends on: 💡 optical movement of data rather than purely electrical scaling.
>
> Smaller pure-play names like: ⚡ $LASE ⚡ Ayar Labs (private) ⚡ Lightmatter (private)
>
> represent the more speculative frontier.
>
> Higher risk. Potentially enormous upside.
>
> Especially if optical interconnect adoption accelerates faster than expected.
>
> Emphasis
>
> In photonics the bottlenecks are: ⚠️ optical integration ⚠️ laser systems ⚠️ advanced packaging ⚠️ thermal efficiency ⚠️ networking infrastructure
>
> The defense angle matters enormously too.
>
> Photonics is not just about AI chatbots.
>
> It increasingly affects: 🛰 satellite systems 🎯 targeting infrastructure 📡 radar systems ⚔ electronic warfare 🤖 autonomous drones
>
> This is becoming strategic infrastructure.
>
> Another major theme:
>
> Photonics helps reduce energy intensity.
>
> This becomes critical because hyperscale AI now collides directly with: ⚡ grid shortages 💧 water scarcity 🔥 cooling constraints 🛢 diesel stress
>
> The physical economy increasingly constrains digital expansion.
>
> We have repeatedly emphasized:
>
> The future AI race may not simply be about: “Who has the best model?”
>
> It may become: “Who can physically power and cool computation?”
>
> Photonics helps solve that problem.
>
> This is why the market increasingly rewards: 🏗 infrastructure ⚡ utilities 💧 cooling 🧲 critical minerals 💡 photonic efficiency
>
> The AI story is becoming deeply industrial.
>
> The broader implication is profound:
>
> Photonics may ultimately do to traditional electronics… …what the internet did to analog communication.
>
> The infrastructure layer itself changes.
>
> But the transition also accelerates concentration.
>
> Only a narrowing circle of: 🏢 hyperscalers 🏦 mega-cap firms 🏭 industrial suppliers ⚔ defense-linked infrastructure players
>
> …may fully benefit.
>
> The K-shape deepens.
>
> The irony is striking:
>
> The AI revolution was originally marketed as democratizing technology.
>
> Instead it increasingly centralizes: ⚡ compute ⚡ infrastructure ⚡ capital ⚡ energy access ⚡ photonic capability
>
> into fewer hands.
>
> We believe the market still underestimates how quickly photonics may become unavoidable.
>
> Because the problem is no longer theoretical.
>
> The electrical system itself is hitting physical limits.
>
> The final takeaway:
>
> The next generation of AI winners may not simply be software companies.
>
> They may be the firms controlling: 💡 light transmission ⚡ power efficiency 🔥 thermal management 🏗 optical infrastructure
>
> The future of computing increasingly belongs to photonics.
>

### Andiamo (@andiamonow)
_Fri Jun 05 19:35:02 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 263 · ↻ 39 · 💬 12 · [open on X](https://x.com/andiamonow/status/2062981542767407527)

> 🚨 CONFIRMED via Finansinspektionen (Swedish FSA): JPMorgan Chase & Co. just crossed the 5% ownership threshold in $SIVE.
>
> Official filing:
> → Holder: JPMorgan Chase & Co.
> → Transaction date: June 2, 2026 (same day as the GlobalFoundries announcement)
> → Reason for flagging: "Köp" (BUY)
> → Pre-transaction position: 0 shares
> → Post-transaction position: 16,098,583 shares / 5.25008% of total voting rights
>
> Position structure:
> → J.P. Morgan Securities plc (UK entity): 15,916,852 voting rights — 5.19%
> → J.P. Morgan Securities LLC (US entity): 181,731 voting rights — 0.06%
> → Direct shares: 10,049,558 (3.14% of total shares)
> → Cash-settled instruments (likely swaps): 6,049,025 share equivalents
>
> Why this is structurally significant:
>
> Swedish law requires mandatory disclosure when crossing the 5% ownership threshold. JPMorgan went from ZERO to 5.25% on June 2. The flagging reason filed with the FSA was explicitly "Köp" (Buy) — not custody, not market-making inventory. This is a deliberate institutional position.
>
> The timing is what makes it remarkable:
>
> June 2 was the same day GlobalFoundries announced the silicon photonics reference design partnership and $SIVE moved +50-70%.
>
> Three possible reads:
> JPM was positioned beforehand and captured the move
>
> JPM built the position aggressively into and after the news.
>
> JPM is positioning ahead of the Nasdaq NY listing in an underwriter / placement agent role
>
> All three are bullish. The third would be the most strategically significant — tier-1 US investment banks don't take 5% positions in Swedish micro-caps without strategic context.
>
> Connecting back to the "zero institutional ownership" post earlier this week:
>
> Five days ago: $SIVE had zero US institutional 13F filings.
>
> Today: the world's largest investment bank discloses a 5%+ position triggered by a "Buy" transaction.
>
> The institutional layer that was missing has started forming.
> The composition tells you it's sophisticated:
> 6 million of the 16 million share-equivalents are in cash-settled derivatives. The rest is direct shares. This is the kind of structured position you set up when you're a major capital markets player preparing for a multi-event sequence — index inclusions, dual listing, sector rotation.
>
> JPMorgan doesn't take 5% positions in $2-3B Swedish micro-caps because they're bored.
>
> $SIVE just got its first major Wall Street institutional anchor.
>
> $SIVE

### Data Fondamental (@datafondamental)
_Fri Jun 05 21:26:30 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/datafondamental/status/2063009594348130317)

> #AnalyseAction - Sivers Semiconductors (SIVE)
>
> On en parle énormément en ce moment, plus haut historique à 110 SEK le 3 juin, environ +60% sur la semaine. Mais déjà deux grosses séances de baisse : -9% hier, encore -9% aujourd'hui à la clôture. On pose les chiffres avant de suivre le momentum.
>
> Le profil :
> Small cap suédoise (Stockholm), spécialiste des réseaux de lasers pour l'optique intégrée des datacenters IA. Cœur de la thèse : la bascule du cuivre vers l'optique (CPO).
>
> Les chiffres (5 juin : 78,80 SEK) :
> Capi ~23 Md SEK. 
> CA 2025 : 360,8 M SEK (+33%). 
> Résultat net : -186,5 M SEK, marge -52%. P/S ~83x. 
> Pas de dividende. Une boîte valorisée plus de 80 fois ses ventes, et pas rentable.
>
> Pourquoi ça flambe (et pourquoi ça corrige) ?
> Deux catalyseurs réels : l'extension du partenariat avec Ayar Labs (lasers Sivers dans la source SuperNova) et la collaboration toute fraîche avec GlobalFoundries, qui intègre ses lasers dans ses designs de référence silicon photonics. Validation par un fondeur majeur, c'est du concret. À noter, certains arguments avancés par @aleabitoreddit sur le rôle de chokepoint laser de Sivers sont d'ailleurs assez intéressants sur le fond. Mais après un tel run, la moindre prise de bénéfices fait très mal, d'où les deux séances rouges.
>
> La cotation à New York :
> Sivers évalue une double cotation au Nasdaq New York (annoncée le 16 avril), tout en gardant son siège en Suède. Ça impose une mise à niveau comptable aux normes PCAOB, dont la certification serait le dernier obstacle avant l'entrée au Nasdaq. Vrai catalyseur potentiel (liquidité, base d'investisseurs US). 
>
> Réserve importante : l'autorité suédoise enquête sur un possible délit d'initié lié à la fuite du projet via un compte anonyme. Tant que ce nuage n'est pas levé, il pèse sur le titre.
>
> Le point noir des résultats :
> T1 2026 : CA en baisse de 22% sur un an. Mais pipeline d'opportunités à 799 M$ (+77% depuis fin 2025) et production LiDAR prévue au T4. Le CA recule pendant que la promesse grossit. Toute la valo repose sur la conversion de ce pipeline.
>
> Mon avis :
> Bonne boîte, meilleur thème du cycle actuel, mais valo déconnectée du présent et risque réglementaire ouvert. Le profil qui peut continuer à monter sur le momentum et corriger violemment au premier accroc (deux séances à -9% d'affilée le rappellent). 
>
> Transparence : j'en détiens, et je l'achète directement sur la bourse suédoise en SEK (et non via l'OTC US). Et c'est pour ça que je m'oblige à rester lucide. À ce prix, j'achète une histoire et un calendrier de catalyseurs, pas des fondamentaux.
>
> Et vous, vous jouez la cotation US et le pipeline, ou la valo et le risque vous semblent intenables ?
>
> Ceci n'est en aucun cas un conseil en investissement, faites vos propres recherches.

### Ryan sikorski (@Ryansikorski10)
_Fri Jun 05 22:02:42 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 17 · ↻ 7 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/Ryansikorski10/status/2063018701931134996)

> HIGH–PULSE-ENERGY FEMTOSECOND MODE-LOCKED LASERS FOR ON CHIP OPTICAL AMPLIFICATION
>
> Over the past decades, extensive efforts have been devoted to developing photonic integrated circuit-based mode-locked lasers that are compact, scalable, and compatible with further on-chip functionalities. Yet, existing implementations fall short of pulse energies required for their subsequent uses in nonlinear applications. THE FIRST MODE-LOCKED LASER THAT OVERCOMES THIS LIMITATION IN LOW-LOSS ERBIUM-DOPED SILICON NITRIDE PHOTONIC INTEGRATED CIRCUITS.
>
> On-chip optical amplification
>
> Because the need for faster chips is expected to see a shift from electronics- to photonics-based technologies, erbium ions could form the basis for amplification in optical integrated circuits. We apply ion implantation to ultralow–loss silicon nitride (Si3N4) photonic integrated circuits, WHICH ARE ABLE TO INCREASE THE SOLITON MICROCOMB OUTPUT POWER BY 100 TIMES, achieving power requirements for low-noise photonic microwave generation and wavelength-division multiplexing optical communications. 
>
> OPERATING IN THE CONTINUOUS-WAVE REGIME and PROVIDING LARGE OPTICAL GAIN IN THE TELECOMMUNICATION BANDS, the results are promising for device (human) applications. —ISO
>
> Endowing Si3N4 photonic integrated circuits WITH GAIN ENABLES THE MINIATURIZATION OF VARIOUS FIBER-BASED DEVICES such as HIGH–PULSE-ENERGY FEMTOSECOND MODE-LOCKED LASERS.
>
> https://t.co/YQyK4yDqj8
>
> The laser is based on the Mamyshev oscillator architecture [8, 9],https://t.co/sgQSd01Yzd which employs alternating spectral filtering & self-phase modulation for mode-locking. It delivers a 176 MHz stream of pulses w/ nanojoule energy, comparable to fiber lasers & surpassing previous photonic integrated sources by more than two orders of magnitude. The output pulses exhibit excellent coherence, can be linearly compressed to 147 fs & directly drive a 1.5-octave-spanning supercontinuum in an integrated waveguide. 
>
> https://t.co/aQKEw7b6le

### くえるじゃん (@Kuerujan)
_Fri Jun 05 23:58:52 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 1 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/Kuerujan/status/2063047935626276996)

> AI半導体投資日報_260606_朝刊
>
> ■朝刊の見取り図
> ・前回夕刊以降の更新で一番重要なのは、AI半導体の実需が強いまま、株価、電力、資源、政策、企業AI ROIの側で検証圧力が上がったこと。
> ・NVIDIA Vera Rubin向けHBM4では、Samsung Electronics、SK hynix、Micronが認定済みで生産中と報じられた。
> ・BroadcomのAI売上は強い。それでも半導体株は急落した。市場は需要の有無ではなく、期待値、金利、長期target、粗利率、顧客集中を見た。
> ・AIデータセンターは、電力、水、土地、冷却、microgrid、費用回収の問題として扱う必要が強まった。
> ・台湾、韓国掲示板、欧州政策の細い観測点は、価値配分がGPU/HBMだけに閉じないことを補強した。
> ・朝刊の結論は明確。AI需要は消えていない。投資では、強い実需をそのまま高リターンへ変換せず、供給制約、導入制約、価格転嫁、織り込み度を分けて確認する。
>
> ■HBM4三社認定は供給リスク低下だが、配分は未確定
> ・NVIDIA CEO Jensen Huangが、Vera Rubin向けHBM4でSamsung Electronics、SK hynix、Micronの三社がqualifiedでproduction中と述べたと報じられた。
> ・この材料は、Vera Rubin世代のHBM4供給網が単一サプライヤー依存から三社体制へ広がる確認材料である。NVIDIA側には、ramp時の供給選択肢と価格交渉余地が増える。
> ・一方で、公式なvolume allocation、層数、容量、速度、電圧、歩留まり、ASP、LTA条件は未開示である。SK hynix、Samsung、Micronの収益配分をこの報道だけで定量化しない。
> ・HBM4の供給力は、DRAM stackだけで決まらない。base die、TSV、bonding、test、CoWoS/2.5D能力、interposer、基板、液冷、電源、ラック組立が同時に必要になる。
> ・投資では、HBM4認定をメモリ企業の強気材料として見る。同時に、NVIDIAの調達分散が将来の価格交渉、HBM5移行、通常DRAM wafer配分へどう効くかを追う。
>
> ■Broadcom後の急落は需要減速ではなく期待値調整
> ・Reutersは、Broadcom決算後に米国上場チップメーカーの時価総額が大きく消え、PHLX Semiconductor Indexも急落したと報じた。
> ・重要なのは、BroadcomのAI半導体売上が弱かったわけではない点である。BroadcomのAI semiconductor revenueは高成長を続けている。
> ・市場が見たのは、7月期ガイダンス、2027年AI revenue target据え置き、custom AI chip需要の上振れ余地、粗利率、顧客集中、金利上昇による評価倍率の圧縮である。
> ・これはAI半導体テーマの弱気転換ではない。強い決算でも、事前期待がさらに高い場合は株価が下がる。AI株は実需テーマであると同時に、遠い将来利益を織り込む長期成長株である。
> ・確認すべき指標は、AI acceleratorとAI networkingの内訳、主要顧客、gross margin、HBM/CoWoS/基板制約、クラウド側のcapex回収、AIアプリ側の売上化である。
>
> ■AIデータセンターは電力・水・土地で稼働能力が決まる
> ・Axiosの記事は、AIデータセンターの制約を電力だけでなく、水、土地、e-waste、冷却、地域負担へ広げた。
> ・DOE Office of Electricityの記事は、AIデータセンターや先端産業の大口負荷に対して、microgrid、stand-alone bridge、grid-connected support、蓄電、需要応答、費用回収が重要になることを示した。
> ・DOEは、データセンター電力使用量が2014年の58TWhから2023年の176TWhへ増え、2028年には325TWhから580TWhへ増える見通しも示した。単一サイトが最大4.5GWを要求する例もある。
> ・この論点は半導体需要に二面で効く。系統接続や地域合意が遅れれば、GPU/HBM出荷がクラウド売上へ変わる時期は後ろ倒しになる。一方で、変圧器、ケーブル、蓄電、microgrid制御、冷却、水処理、電力ソフトウェアには新しい需要が生まれる。
> ・データセンターcapexを読むときは、チップ発注だけでなく、接続時期、電源構成、PUE/WUE、地域許認可、料金負担、負荷柔軟性を同じ画面で確認する。
>
> ■台湾・韓国・欧州の細い材料が価値配分を広げる
> ・Taipei Timesは、TSMC C.C. WeiのAI需要発言を、先端チップ、装置、装置部品、メモリ、packaging、testing、cooling systems、power supplyの同時制約として伝えた。
> ・TWSE/COMPUTEX記事では、Nanya、Alchip、Unimicron、Msscorps関連発言が、DRAM bit growth、custom AI chip、ABF substrate、packaging materials、materials analysisへ需要を分解した。
> ・DCInsideのSoCAMM投稿は、Rubin NVL72の容量縮小観測を、メモリ容量減少ではなくmodule count、substrate specification、rack shipmentで読む視点を示した。掲示板材料のため、公式仕様と部品表の確認が必要である。
> ・Bits&ChipsのEU Chips Act 2.0記事は、欧州政策が前工程fab偏重から、需要側施策、成熟半導体、設計、3D packaging、装置、specialty materials、integrated photonicsへ広がると整理した。
> ・EvertiqのTessalia記事は、Foxconn、Radiall、ThalesのフランスSiP拠点を、高信頼実装、防衛、通信、医療向けの主権能力形成として位置づける材料である。AIサーバー直結ではないが、欧州の後工程政策を見る入口になる。
>
> ■企業AIのROIは半導体需要の反証条件になる
> ・THE DECODERが紹介したBain調査では、AI cost savingsを測定した企業の約40%が10%未満の削減にとどまった。一方で、9割の企業はAI投資を増やす計画を持つ。
> ・この材料はAIブームの否定ではない。企業はAIをやめていない。問題は、agent導入が人間の承認、データアクセス、監査、権限管理、業務設計で詰まることにある。
> ・CloudflareのVoidZero買収は、AI codingがモデルAPIだけでなく、Vite、build、test、Workers、D1、R2、edge deployment、intent-based infrastructureへ需要を広げる観測点である。
> ・ユーザー提供資料のAIバブル論は、技術失速ではなく、鉄道バブル型の回収時期ずれ、航空業界型の価格競争、用途別棲み分け、先行者優位プロダクトの有無を論点にした。
> ・半導体側の受注が強くても、最終需要側のROIが広く確認できなければ、クラウドcapexとモデル企業の投資回収は脆くなる。逆にROIが確認されれば、推論需要は一段長く続く。
>
> ■朝刊の確認ポイント
> ・HBM4は、認定済みという事実と、配分・歩留まり・ASP未確認を分ける。
> ・Broadcom後の急落は、実需減速ではなく期待値、金利、粗利率、顧客集中の検証として扱う。
> ・AIデータセンターは、GPU/HBM発注と稼働開始を分け、電力、水、土地、地域合意、microgridを追う。
> ・台湾・韓国・欧州材料は、ABF、SoCAMM、packaging materials、materials analysis、SiP、integrated photonicsへ価値連鎖を広げる。
> ・企業AIは、agent発表よりも、data access、human-in-the-loop、監査、task completion、顧客ROIで見る。

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKFrKbcbQAAqmHP.jpg

### The Asian Investor (@asianinvestors)
_Mon Jun 08 19:07:32 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 48 · ↻ 1 · 💬 4 · [open on X](https://x.com/asianinvestors/status/2064061784655626519)

> For those just starting to follow $SIVE, here's a breakdown of their previous earnings report 
>
> On the surface it looked rough.
>
> But underneath it was a 2027 story. Quick breakdown
>
> The "ugly":
>
> Revenue 61.9m SEK, down 22% YoY
> Gross margin caved to 6.8% (was 11.7%)
> Adj EBITDA -13.8m, worse than last year
> Cash down to 26.6m from 73.5m a year ago
>
> They burned ~49m in operating cash in a single quarter. That’s the real headline.
>
> It gets spicier. To stay funded they:
>
> Raised ~125m SEK in April (more dilution, share count 269m to 311m YoY)
> Took a $17m loan facility at 12% / 10.85%
>
> That is expensive money. The balance sheet quality got worse this quarter.
>
> But here’s why I’m still holding:
>
> The revenue miss is timing, not lost business. North America sales halved purely from US defense budget approvals slipping into H2. Europe and Asia actually grew. Demand isn’t the problem.
>
> The bull case is the pipeline:
>
> Opportunity pipeline up 77% YTD to $799M
>
> Jabil collab on a 1.6T pluggable transceiver (AI datacenter validation)
> LIDAR auto ramp on track for Q4 2026
> Multiple 2027 ramps stacking: FWA, defense, SATCOM
>
> So the setup is simple. This quarter they got paid in pipeline and diluted in equity at the same time.
>
> The whole thesis rides on the 2027 ramps actually converting to orders. If they slip the way Q1 revenue did, the cash position forces more dilution at worse terms
>
> Now post earnings, we've gotten more validation. Still speculative but derisked. 
>
> GFS deal: SIVE’s lasers are now the reference design inside GFS’s silicon photonics platform. So when GFS sells photonics chips to data center customers, SIVE rides along as the light source. Big validation, but no confirmed revenue yet.
>
> Ayar x NVIDIA: Ayar’s CPO just got plugged into NVIDIA’s NVLink Fusion ecosystem. SIVE makes the lasers inside Ayar’s SuperNova product. So NVIDIA scales AI factories → Ayar ships more CPO modules → SIVE ships more lasers. Classic upstream pull-through.

### Cyberpunk Sense 👑 (@napoleon21st)
_Mon Jun 08 19:13:11 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 57 · ↻ 9 · 💬 9 · [open on X](https://x.com/napoleon21st/status/2064063206776254486)

> MY PORTFOLIO EXPLAINED
> I have been meticulously building a portfolio based on the thesis that the Physical AI revolution is upon us.
> I have chosen each of these companies, both for what they do and for providing asymmetrical return opportunity to investors. 
>
> $SIVE  Sivers Semiconductors 
> Sivers makes high-frequency radio frequency (RF) millimeter-wave (mmWave) transceivers and advanced optical semiconductors through its Wireless and Photonics divisions. In the AI ecosystem, the company is a critical enabler of next-generation data centers, collaborating with foundry giants like GlobalFoundries to integrate its laser arrays into silicon photonics and co-packaged optics (CPO) platforms to eliminate interconnect bandwidth bottlenecks for massive workloads. Concurrently, its mmWave technologies supply high-speed wireless connectivity for satellite communications, 5G telecom, and edge infrastructure, providing the high-throughput network backbone necessary for real-time edge AI coordination and smart cities.  
>
> $LPK LPKF Laser & Electronics 
> LPKF makes high-precision, laser-based micro-material manufacturing systems, headlined by its proprietary Laser Induced Deep Etching (LIDE) technology. As conventional organic substrates struggle with heavy thermal loads and warpage from massive chiplet integration, LPKF provides the precise tools needed to drill defect-free through-glass vias (TGVs) at aspect ratios up to 1:50 with zero micro-cracks. This specialized capability directly underpins advanced hardware and high-performance computing, enabling leading chipmakers to scale up substrate sizes, integrate high-bandwidth memory (HBM), and implement in-package microfluidic cooling for the next wave of physical AI chips.  
>
> $ACCON Acconeer
> Acconeer makes ultra-low-power, miniature 60 GHz Pulsed Coherent Radar (PCR) sensors that fuse millimeter-level depth precision with an exceptionally small spatial footprint. Within Edge AI and robotics, Acconeer’s chips allow tiny, battery-constrained hardware to execute real-time motion tracking, presence detection, and material or surface classification without relying on heavy cloud computation or invasive optical cameras. By deploying deep learning interfaces that compile models directly onto its integrated microcontrollers, the company provides robots, drones, and consumer devices with the localized spatial awareness required for autonomous navigation, gesture control, and power-efficient smart presence sensing.  
>
> $SILC  Silicom 
> Silicom designs and manufactures high-performance networking and data infrastructure hardware, including server network interface cards (NICs), programmable FPGA-based acceleration cards, SmartNICs, and edge switches. The company anchors Edge AI and smart systems by offloading heavy encryption, data compression, and packet-routing tasks from host CPUs, allowing decentralized AI infrastructure to maintain ultra-low latency and maximum data throughput. Operating primarily via design wins with cybersecurity firms, hyperscalers, and telcos, Silicom enables the secure, low-latency processing fabrics required for distributed AI inference networks and 5G/6G open radio access network (O-RAN) rollouts.  
>
> $GAPW-B Gapwaves
> Gapwaves develops and fabricates specialized, millimeter-wave antennas utilizing its patented gap-waveguide technology. This low-loss, cost-efficient hardware is engineered to maximize the resolution, beam direction, and overall range of high-frequency radar systems without increasing power consumption. Gapwaves fits squarely into the autonomous systems and smart city landscapes by supplying Tier-1 automotive partners with the structural building blocks for next-generation ADAS (Advanced Driver Assistance Systems), enabling autonomous vehicles, industrial transport robots, and urban traffic monitors to build reliable, high-definition models of their surroundings under any weather condition.
>
> $SEYE Smart Eye
> Smart Eye makes computer-vision hardware and software platforms dedicated to Human Insight AI, tracking eye gaze, facial expressions, and head movements in real time. The company’s primary footprint is in the automotive sector, where its edge-based Driver Monitoring Systems (DMS) and interior cabin sensing modules identify operator distraction, drowsiness, and cognitive load to comply with global safety mandates. This technology bridges the human-machine interface across smart transportation and autonomous vehicles, while its subsidiaries (like Affectiva) extend this technology into emotion AI, which is increasingly utilized in behavioral research, aerospace simulators, and interactive robotics.
>
> $AMBA Ambarella
> Ambarella builds ultra-low-power, high-efficiency system-on-chip (SoC) vision and radar processors built on its algorithm-first CVflow artificial intelligence architecture. Its chips, like the 4nm CV7 and the high-compute N1 series, serve as the localized brain for Edge AI, industrial robotics, and smart city infrastructure by running complex convolutional and transformer neural networks simultaneously. By integrating advanced image signal processing, hardware-accelerated video encoding, and native neural network computation on a single die, Ambarella allows security cameras, aerial drones, and autonomous mobile robots (AMRs) to execute edge-based multi-sensor perception, visual odometry, and real-time SLAM (Simultaneous Localization and Mapping) entirely disconnected from the cloud.
>
> $OUST Ouster
>  Ouster designs and manufactures high-resolution 3D digital LiDAR sensors alongside integrated perception suites, following its strategic combination with Stereolabs' ZED camera technology. By embedding native color and precise spatial mapping directly onto its proprietary silicon architecture, Ouster creates an end-to-end sensing platform for Physical AI. This hardware acts as the primary sensory organ for humanoid robotics, warehouse automation, autonomous mining fleets, and smart city infrastructure (via its BlueCity traffic management software), delivering low-latency, resilient environmental data that allows machines to map, track, and safely navigate complex physical spaces.
>
> $AMZN Amazon
> Within the AI and robotics verticals, Amazon develops custom infrastructure silicon—such as its proprietary Trainium and Inferentia acceleration chips—while engineering vast, automated logistics systems for its global fulfillment network. The company is a pioneer in warehouse robotics, deploying fleets of fully autonomous mobile robots like Proteus and intelligent manipulation systems like Sparrow to streamline its supply chain via machine learning and reinforcement learning. On the edge, Amazon implements localized AI and natural language processing through consumer ecosystems like Alexa, Ring, and the Astro home robot, establishing a ubiquitous presence across cloud AI architecture, industrial automation, and smart home systems.
>
> $ELMT Elmet Group
> Elmet Group fabricates precision-engineered components and high-power radio frequency (RF) or microwave equipment, operating through its Critical Materials Components and Engineered Microwave Products divisions. Specializing in the custom manufacturing of refractory metals like pure tungsten and molybdenum, Elmet supplies the foundational, high-durability hardware components required for advanced semiconductor fabrication, aerospace systems, and defense electronics. It fits into the advanced hardware and AI supply chain by delivering the critical thermal management substrates, ion implantation shielding, and robust RF distribution modules necessary to manufacture and run high-energy compute chips.
>
> $TRT Trio-Tech International 
> Trio-Tech provides semiconductor back-end testing services and manufactures heavy-duty reliability equipment, including customized burn-in boards, wet process stations, and environmental testing chambers. The company serves as a vital gatekeeper for advanced hardware reliability, validating that complex chips can withstand severe thermal and electrical stress without failing prior to commercial rollout. Driven by the massive ramp-up in next-generation computing architectures, Trio-Tech directly supports AI and smart automotive expansion by stress-testing high-performance GPUs, CPUs, and electric vehicle (EV) electronics across its key facilities in Southeast Asia.
>
> $HLIT Harmonic
> Harmonic produces virtualized broadband access networks and software-based cloud video delivery infrastructure, known for solutions like its VOS360 cloud platform and cOS applications. The company embeds AI into smart systems by leveraging Content-Aware Encoding (CAE) algorithms and dynamic ad-insertion technologies to process mass media streams at the network edge, squeezing bandwidth requirements by up to 50% without compromising visual quality. This positions Harmonic as a fundamental utility provider for edge systems and smart cities, optimizing the heavy data pipelines that distribute live television, ultra-high-definition streaming, and localized broadband connectivity at scale.

### Con (@__Con_)
_Mon Jun 08 19:28:47 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 17 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/__Con_/status/2064067131327877327)

> $ASYS vs $VECO 
>
> Which one's better?
>
> Here's a review:
>
> $ASYS just printed 31% y/y revenue growth in its latest quarter, expanded gross margins to 47.7% on the shift to higher-ASP AI packaging products, and moved solidly back into profitability. It trades at roughly 4x sales.
>
> $VECO trades at a similar 3.7-4x sales. It is larger ($2.4B market cap vs $320M), more established, and carries exposure to the hot silicon photonics wave for AI optical interconnects. Both operate in the advanced packaging and process equipment layer that enables AI GPUs, chiplets, and photonics.
>
> So why nearly identical multiples when one is smaller, growing faster in the core AI segment right now, and printing much higher gross margins?
>
> Let's walk through it.
>
> $ASYS specializes in thermal processing solutions: precision reflow ovens, belt furnaces, and related tools that handle the critical solder reflow and thermal steps in advanced semiconductor packaging for AI GPUs, chiplets, and high-power devices. This is the specialized “assembly oven” layer that enables high-yield, high-throughput packaging of complex multi-die architectures.
>
> $VECO offers a broader set of process tools: wet processing/clean/etch platforms (recently qualified for new advanced packaging applications), laser spike annealing, ion beam deposition, plus MOCVD and tools supporting silicon photonics fabrication. Complementary steps in the packaging and photonics manufacturing flow.
>
> They are not direct one-for-one competitors on every product, but they sit adjacent in the advanced packaging equipment supply chain for AI. Leading OSATs and IDMs building next-gen AI infrastructure often use tools from both (plus others) to complete the packaging and optical engine builds. You need robust thermal/reflow capability as part of the flows that VECO’s wet/anneal tools support in other steps.
>
> In fact, strong AI packaging demand is pulling on the entire equipment ecosystem.
>
> Here is why the market prices them so closely:
>
> $VECO is the bigger, more diversified platform with scale across semiconductor, silicon photonics (AI optical I/O), data storage recovery, and scientific markets. More institutional coverage, better liquidity, and a “portfolio” story that captures multiple AI infrastructure vectors.
>
> $ASYS is the smaller, more concentrated pure-play on the thermal/reflow step specifically for AI advanced packaging. Cleaner narrative, less exposed to cyclical data storage, but it carries the natural microcap liquidity and coverage discount.
>
> $ASYS has already executed the mix shift. AI-related revenue is now >30% of its Thermal Processing segment and expected to exceed 40% soon, driving gross margins from deeply negative territory last year to 47%+ today with high incremental margins as volume scales.
>
> $ASYS runs an asset-light model with focused subsidiaries and recently raised capital to accelerate growth and M&A. Order momentum and backlog are building on AI packaging demand.
>
> That explains a lot of the similarity in multiples. But here is what $ASYS brings that creates the opportunity:
>
> - Superior margin profile and operating leverage right now. The AI packaging reflow products carry high ASPs and high gross margins. As that mix climbs further, margins expand with limited opex growth.
>
> - More direct, leveraged exposure to the AI GPU/chiplet packaging capex wave. This is one of the most capacity-constrained and critical parts of the AI buildout. Advanced thermal processes are essential for yield and reliability in high-density, high-power packages.
>
> - Smaller base + re-rating torque. Proving sustained growth and 45%+ gross margins in a high-demand niche can support a move to 6-8x sales (still reasonable for this profile). That would be substantial upside from current levels. VECO already prices in more of its scale and photonics breadth.
>
> - Clean U.S.-based positioning serving leading global packaging houses ramping AI products, with no China manufacturing overhang that affects some other names in the broader chain.
>
> The takeaway and my thoughts:
>
> I am not saying $ASYS deserves a massive premium to $VECO (but I do think this is the case lol). Scale, diversification (including photonics), and platform breadth at VECO justify a similar multiple.
>
> But two names in the AI advanced packaging/photonics equipment ecosystem, both around 4x sales, where the smaller one is growing faster in its core AI segment, has dramatically higher and still-expanding gross margins, a cleaner focused story, and more asymmetric upside from here… that is worth sitting with.
>
> $ASYS also has a more concentrated bet on the exact packaging equipment step seeing intense pull from every major AI accelerator designer moving to chiplet architectures.
>
> What do you think?
>
> Do you think $ASYS offers better risk/reward than $VECO (the larger peer in the same niche)?
>
> I certainly do.
>
> $ASYS is also breaking out of a 30 year support/resistance channel looking to breakout and use this as support.
>
> $VECO already had its breakout (still seems like it wants to go up, just not as much as $ASYS here).
>
> That's why I am long $ASYS.
>
> If you guys got any other tickers that you want me to compare to each other, send them down below.

### Anton (@seahorse_anton)
_Mon Jun 08 20:22:25 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 4 · ↻ 0 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/seahorse_anton/status/2064080630493700218)

> LPKF Laser & Electronics SE (XETRA Germany: LPK) . They are a highly specialized German high-tech engineering and photonics company that builds precision, laser-based manufacturing systems.
>
> Essentially, they create the complex laser machines that other companies use to build microchips, solar panels, and circuit boards.
> The Quick Profile
>
> Headquarters: Garbsen, Germany (near Hanover).
> Founded: 1976 (they started out making mechanical tools for prototyping circuit boards before moving heavily into lasers).
> Size: Publicly traded on the Frankfurt Stock Exchange, with around 700 to 750 employees globally.
>
> What Do They Actually Make?
> Instead of making consumer electronics, LPKF operates behind the scenes in four main industrial sectors:
>
> 1/ Advanced Semiconductor Packaging (The Big Growth Area): They are currently making major waves in the microchip industry with a patented technology called LIDE (Laser Induced Deep Etching). As silicon chips hit their physical limits, the industry is shifting toward using glass as a base (interposer) for next-gen AI and high-performance computing chips. LIDE allows companies to micro-drill and structure glass without causing micro-cracks or defects.
>
> 2/ Electronics & Circuit Boards: They make laser depaneling systems (glorified, ultra-precise laser cutters) that slice fragile, flexible printed circuit boards (PCBs) out of larger sheets during manufacturing without damaging the tiny components. They also sell "Rapid Prototyping" benchtop lasers to universities and research labs so engineers can print custom circuit boards in-house.
> 3/ Laser Plastic Welding: They build machines that use lasers to fuse plastic parts together seamlessly. This is huge in medical devices and automotive manufacturing (like EV cooling systems)—especially with their recent "Absorbing-to-Absorbing" technology, which allows two dark, laser-absorbing plastics to be welded together without needing a transparent layer.
> 4/ Solar Energy: They develop laser scribing systems used to score and structure thin-film solar cells, increasing their efficiency. They are currently pivoting these machines to support next-generation perovskite solar cells.
> 1. Core Physics of the Disruption (LIDE® Technology)As an AI semiconductor specialist and physicist, the document analyzes the fundamental breakdown of organic packaging substrates when handling multi-GHz signals required by modern LLM compute clusters.The Problem: Conventional substrate materials experience high dielectric loss and mechanical warpage under the severe thermal fluctuations generated by massive tensor processing units.  The Solution: Moving to a glass core substrate. LPKF owns a patented chemical-physical process called LIDE® (Laser-Induced Deep Etching).  The Physics: The system utilizes precise, multi-photon laser absorption to alter the chemical microstructure of technical glasses (such as borosilicate) locally without injecting thermal shock or micro-cracks into the surrounding matrix. A subsequent selective wet-etching process attacks the modified glass at an accelerated selectivity ratio of up to 1:50.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKUWBejWcAAMBKI.jpg

> $NVDA CEO Basically Claims That the Memory Shortages Aren't Ending Anytime Soon
>
> "The memory market has recently been shrouded in negative rumors that "Nvidia has halved its use of memory modules in Vera Rubin server racks." However, Nvidia CEO Jensen Huang came forward to refute the rumors, stating that 'there is no end in sight to the memory shortage," and announced that the company will purchase more memory from SK Hynix. The two companies will also work together to develop next-generation memory technology.
>
> Analysts point out that Huang's remarks dispelled rumors of a sharp decline in Nvidia's memory usage, providing reassurance to memory manufacturers such as Nanya Technology (2408) and Winbond (2344) regarding their future prospects. Nvidia's plan to purchase more SK Hynix high-bandwidth memory (HBM) and collaborate on next-generation technology development will likely benefit Taiwanese manufacturers, particularly TSMC's subsidiary, Creative Labs (3443), which is working with SK Hynix to further develop HBM4-related ASIC-side IP.
>
> Huang pointed out that the current demand in the AI ​​industry far exceeds the supply. The supply chain, from wafer manufacturing and advanced packaging to silicon photonics technology, is in a state of supply shortage. The demand is so large that it is difficult to meet. He predicts that this situation will continue for many years. In addition, AI infrastructure is still in a stage of rapid expansion, and there are no signs of the global data center investment boom cooling down.
>
> When asked about the rumor that "Nvidia's Vera Rubin server rack memory module usage has been halved," Huang refuted it, emphasizing that "there is no end in sight to the memory shortage."

### Rosanna Prestia, MBA (@RosannaInvests)
_Mon Jun 08 22:26:48 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 30 · ↻ 4 · 💬 4 · [open on X](https://x.com/RosannaInvests/status/2064111930613379076)

> 🚨The AI chips are useless without it. 
>
> A GPU is just expensive silicon until you can move data between them at the speed AI demands and that connection layer is becoming the real bottleneck.
>
> That's the $CRDO thesis. And I've been long for a while.
>
> $CRDO built its name on copper connectivity -> the SerDes, DSPs, and active electrical cables that move data between AI chips. The one open question was always what happens when the industry shifts from copper to optical. With the DustPhotonics acquisition, Credo brought silicon photonics in-house and now owns the full connectivity stack: SerDes → DSP → active cables → optical transceivers → silicon photonics, spanning 800G to a 3.2T roadmap. Electrical and optical, end to end.
>
> That's the moat. When Jensen says the future of AI depends on connectivity, this is the layer he means and $CRDO is the pure-play that owns all of it.
>
> The fundamentals: FY26 revenue more than tripled to $1.34B, non-GAAP net income rose 5x to $662M, ~68% gross margins, $1.4B cash and no debt.
>
> $CRDO - run the forward math*👇
>
> → Revenue CAGR (FY26–FY28): ~61%
> → PEG: ~0.52 -> Re-Rate ✨
> → EV/Sales: ~17x FY27 → ~11x FY28
> → Forward P/E: ~65x trailing → ~42x FY27 → ~27x FY28
>
> A company compounding revenue at ~61% with a PEG of ~0.5.
>
> The multiple isn't the story. The growth is. Watch the "expensive" 65x compress as earnings catch up to 42x, then 27x.
>
> “Expensive” on today's numbers. Cheap on where it's going + re-rate.
>
> Everyone's buying the chips.
>
> The chips are useless if you can't connect them.
>
> $CRDO owns the connection. 👀
>
> *Estimated from projections

### chris seekins (@karmaxul)
_Mon Jun 08 23:41:33 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/karmaxul/status/2064130744008454523)

> The country is networked with 200 micron fiberoptic fibers, to move data around the country. I used to make that some years ago. The space station used a smaller micron, I want to say it was 120 micron though it was some years ago. Slot machines use 200 micron. Im not familiar with photonics though sounds fascinating. There are interesting properties regarding nanometers, what light is measured in, and a reverse scale, tHz. Once refined, think of them as reverse scales. 540nm = 540tHz. 360nm = 720tHz. Their balances do some interesting things and I feel will be the future of data processing though not how one may think. Happy to explain if there is interest though I’ll warn you, cryptographers can’t keep up and the average person has no interest. Personally, I think I could teach it to the average eight year old, people are just set in there ways. Once quantum computing becomes a threat, there will be no choice other then to accept it. ### JSCC (@JSCC2020Lee)
_Sun Jun 07 21:29:44 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/JSCC2020Lee/status/2063735183661224433)

> 구리에서 빛으로, 반도체의 한계를 넘는 여정
> 오늘 대화에서는 고성능 반도체 패키징 기술, 특히 HBM(High Bandwidth Memory)의 현재와 미래에 대해 깊이 있는 이야기를 나누었습니다.
> 현재 고속 연산을 담당하는 HBM은 D램을 여러 층 쌓아 올리고, 'TSV(Through-Silicon Via)'라는 미세한 구리 통로를 통해 데이터를 수직으로 전송합니다. 이것은 나노미터 단위의 초정밀 공정이 만들어낸 기적 같은 기술이지만, 데이터 전송량이 늘어날수록 전력 소모와 발열이라는 물리적 한계에 부딪히고 있습니다.
> 과거 우리가 지구촌 인터넷망을 연결할 때 전송 효율을 위해 구리선에서 광섬유로 대전환했던 것처럼, 반도체 패키징의 세계도 결국 '전기'가 아닌 '빛'으로 데이터를 전송하는 광학 기술(CPO, Silicon Photonics)의 시대로 향할 것입니다.
> 하지만 현재 양산 단계에서는 '구리'를 이용한 전기적 연결이 여전히 가장 현실적이고 신뢰성 높은 최선의 방식입니다. 우리는 지금 구리의 시대가 저물고, 빛의 시대가 시작되는 그 기술적 전환점의 한복판에 서 있습니다. 전력과 열이라는 인류의 과제를 해결하기 위한 새로운 소재와 구조 혁신이 계속되고 있는 것입니다.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKPcNW1boAAj91n.jpg

### bubble boi (@bubbleboi)
_Sun Jun 07 21:29:55 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1811 · ↻ 227 · 💬 89 · [open on X](https://x.com/bubbleboi/status/2063735227382677573)

> TSMC fumbles Copackaged optics for the Nth time like some fucking donkeys and now the whole industry is limping towards NPO, and the pod bros who price the entire AI TAM off Nvidia’s BOM line items still can’t actually explain what the problem is. So let me do the engineering for you, since clearly nobody on here will.
>
> The bottleneck was never can you make light go through a waveguide. It’s all fucking thermals which is downstream of packaging. Specifically, how do you get a photonic engine onto the same substrate as a switch ASIC or XPU without your yield falling off a cliff and your reliability failing.
>
> TSMC’s answer is CoWoS where they bolt everything onto one big monolithic silicon interposer. Cute, until you hit the reticle limit and start duct-taping interposers together (CoWoS-S, then -R, then -L, soon -PleaseStop). Every chiplet and HBM stack you add to that single interposer compounds your defect probability and one bad die leads to a five-figure package going into the dumpster. CoWoS is thermally retarded and the whole industry knows this and it’s why capacity “can’t expand” and Jensen is acting like a bouncer in the front of a club choosing who gets pass the velvet rope. 
>
> There is ONLY one company that will make copackaged optics work and expand in the rack… it’s not Lumentum, it’s not Coherent, it’s fucking INTELLLL.
>
> Intel’s EMIB gets rid of a giant reticle limited interposer and replaces it with a tiny silicon bridge that does the high-density coupling locally, exactly where you need it. You localize the hard part and the thermals in one area and your yield is ridiculously high. Comparing EMIB & CoWoS is so funny cause EMIB is north of 95% yield with like 12 reticle size equivalent package while CoWoS falls off a cliff after 5.5 reticles it’s that bad…now imagine adding thermally sensitive photonics.
>
> People don’t know this but Intel has been doing silicon photonics in-house for ~25 years... In 2024 they showed an Optical I/O chiplet doing 2 Tbps bidirectionally at ~5 pJ/bit, with the PIC and EIC co-packaged right against the ASIC and it’s all because of EMIB. And even more critically than that, they’ve actually run the fiber-attach and reliability/test flow to JEDEC-grade standards already, which everyone hand-waves until their links flap in production.
>
> My prediction is clear: Intel will capture over 90% of the copackaged silicon photonics market in the next five years because there is NO ALTERNATIVE.

**Media**

### Marshall Pickett (@Pikithome)
_Sun Jun 07 23:29:56 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Pikithome/status/2063765433686053114)

> How this is positive for $MRVL according to Ai
>
> The genuine read-through for Marvell is the platform validation. SK Hynix is codeveloping memory for NVIDIA Vera Rubin AI supercomputers, Vera CPUs, RTX Spark-powered PCs and Jetson Thor platforms . Marvell already has its own NVIDIA tie-in: back in March 2026, NVIDIA and Marvell announced a strategic partnership connecting Marvell to the NVIDIA AI factory ecosystem through NVLink Fusion, and NVIDIA invested $2 billion in Marvell . Marvell provides custom XPUs and NVLink Fusion–compatible scale-up networking, while NVIDIA provides the Vera CPU, ConnectX NICs, Bluefield DPUs, NVLink interconnect and Spectrum-X switches . So anything that accelerates the Vera Rubin / AI-factory buildout broadly supports demand for the custom silicon, optical interconnect, and networking content Marvell sells into those same racks.
> Notably, Marvell’s own IP portfolio includes custom high-bandwidth memory (HBM), silicon photonics, optical IO, and compute fabric interfaces like PCIe Gen 7  — so a healthier, faster-scaling memory supply chain feeding NVIDIA platforms is a tailwind for the systems Marvell co-designs into.
> The honest counterpoints: this is a memory-maker deal, and Marvell doesn’t make DRAM/HBM cells — it integrates custom HBM into XPUs, so there’s no direct revenue line here. If anything, the bearish framing is that NVIDIA continues to deepen first-party and Korean-memory relationships, and Marvell’s bigger swing factor remains its custom XPU design wins with hyperscalers, not NVIDIA’s memory sourcing. Marvell already guided strongly on its own — it raised its fiscal 2027 and 2028 revenue outlook on exceptional AI bookings across 800G/1.6T optics, Ethernet switches, scale-up optical, DCI modules, and custom XPU solutions  — so this announcement doesn’t change Marvell’s fundamentals.
> Bottom line: mildly positive sentiment read-through (validates the AI-factory/Vera Rubin ramp Marvell is levered to)

### くえるじゃん (@Kuerujan)
_Sun Jun 07 23:58:18 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 7 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/Kuerujan/status/2063772571473244583)

> AI半導体投資日報_260608_朝刊
>
> ■朝刊の見取り図
> ・対象期間は、2026年6月7日夕刊後から6月8日朝まで。
> ・前回夕刊では、電力、冷却、HBM熱設計、アジアマクロ、企業AIの費用規律を扱った。
> ・今朝の焦点は、AI需要そのものではない。
> ・焦点は、AI需要が利益と株式リターンへ変わる条件である。
> ・結論は明確。AI半導体需要は強い。
> ・ただし、投資では、メモリ不足、カスタムシリコン、電力、データセンター資本、企業AI採算、株式供給を同時に見る。
>
> ■メモリ不足はHBMだけで終わらない
> ・Reutersは、NVIDIAと韓国SKグループが6月8日に協力計画を説明する見通しを伝えた。
> ・記事時点では、協力の具体的な範囲は未開示である。
> ・HBM配分、価格、契約期間、前払い、顧客別数量は確認できない。
> ・重要なのは、Jensen Huang氏が不足を広く語った点である。
> ・不足はメモリ単体ではない。wafers、packaging、silicon photonicsを含む供給網全体の問題である。
> ・Vera Rubin向けHBM4では、Samsung、SK hynix、Micronが認定済みかつ生産中とされる。
> ・三社認定は前進である。ただし、供給制約の解消ではない。
> ・DRAM wafer、base die、2.5D実装、基板、熱、テスト、ラック統合は別に確認する。
>
> ■Samsung HBM4Eは一次資料として重要
> ・Samsungは、12層HBM4Eサンプルを主要顧客へ出荷し始めた。
> ・仕様は、48GB、14Gbps pin speed、最大16Gbps、最大3.6TB/s/stackである。
> ・同社は、1c DRAMと4nm logic base dieを使う。
> ・HBM4Eは、DRAM stackだけの製品ではない。
> ・base die、電源網、熱経路、先端パッケージング、顧客認定を含む複合部品である。
> ・ただし、発表はsample shipment段階である。
> ・量産月、採用顧客、出荷数量、ASP、歩留まり、NVIDIA向け配分は未確認である。
> ・Samsungの逆転や供給不足の解消は、まだ断定しない。
>
> ■メモリ価格は受益と原価圧力を同時に生む
> ・Morgan StanleyのMicronとSanDisk見通しは、AI半導体強気論の範囲が広がったことを示す。
> ・強気論はGPUとASICだけではない。
> ・DRAM、NAND、enterprise SSD、資本政策へ広がった。
> ・メモリ不足は、Micron、Samsung、SK hynix、SanDisk、Kioxiaの粗利とFCFには追い風になる。
> ・同じ不足は、クラウド、AIモデル企業、AIアプリ企業、PCメーカーには原価上昇として効く。
> ・価格上昇が強すぎると、需要側は設計を変える。
> ・候補は、KV cache圧縮、低容量構成、NAND/SSD階層化、推論専用ASIC、local/cloud routingである。
> ・韓国DCInsideでは、DDR5価格高騰でSRAMとDRAMの相対価格差が縮み、AIチップがon-chip SRAMを増やす仮説が議論された。
> ・ただし、SRAMは容量密度が低い。off-chip DRAMの単純な代替にはならない。
> ・この議論は数値の根拠ではない。
> ・価値は、メモリ原価がチップ設計とモデル効率化へ圧力をかける点にある。
>
> ■資本市場はAI実需と株式リターンを分ける
> ・Axiosは、AIビジネスの現実として、費用の大きさ、企業ROIの未達、Broadcom期待差、金利負担を挙げた。
> ・これはAI需要の否定ではない。
> ・需要が強くても、EPS、FCF、粗利、資本コスト、評価倍率へ変わるまでに条件がある。
> ・BroadcomのAI半導体売上は強い。
> ・市場は、7月期見通し、2027年以降のvisibility、gross margin、顧客集中、AI networkingのmixを同時に見る。
> ・Bloombergは、SpaceX、Anthropic、OpenAIの大型IPO候補と、AlphabetのAIデータセンター資本調達を扱った。
> ・AI capexを支える資金調達は、半導体需要の追い風である。
> ・同じ資金調達は、希薄化、株式供給増、指数リバランス、AI proxy銘柄の評価低下を生む。
> ・強い実需があっても、株価が同じ強さで動くとは限らない。
>
> ■AI computeは民間資本の商品になった
> ・米国VCと資産運用の発信では、AI computeがインフラ投資商品として扱われている。
> ・BlackstoneとGoogleのTPU Cloud JVは象徴的である。
> ・Blackstoneは50億ドルのinitial equity commitmentを行う。
> ・最初の500MW capacity onlineは2027年に見込まれる。
> ・TPUはGoogle内部のAI ASICだけではない。
> ・外部顧客向けcompute-as-a-serviceと、インフラ資本を組み合わせた商品になった。
> ・ARKは、data center systems investment、accelerated compute、custom silicon、training/inference costを一体で見る。
> ・Menloは、企業AI支出の拡大を示す。
> ・一方で、真のagent architectureはまだ少数である。
> ・多くの本番導入は、固定シーケンスとrouting中心である。
> ・VCとPEの発信は強気になりやすい。
> ・短期受注ではなく、民間資本がどの制約を収益機会と見ているかを見る。
>
> ■オープンモデルとカスタムシリコンは需要の形を変える
> ・open model ecosystemの焦点は、weights公開から広がった。
> ・焦点は、agent execution、post-training、evaluation、serving kernel、local deployment、roboticsへ移った。
> ・Hugging Faceのagent向けCLIは、agentがdataset、job、endpointを扱うときの失敗率とtoken消費を下げる。
> ・Holo3.1は、computer-use agentがlocal/edgeへ寄る可能性を示す。
> ・これはcloud GPU需要を消す材料ではない。
> ・低遅延や機密処理は端末側へ寄る。
> ・重いreasoning、評価、同期、ログ、モデル更新はクラウド側へ残る。
> ・Together AIとNous Researchの効率化は、長文context、KV cache、sparse attentionを軽くする。
> ・効率化はGPU需要を減らす場合もある。
> ・同じGPU fleetで処理できるtask量を増やす場合もある。
> ・AnthropicがOpenAI初期チップ人材を採用した動きも重要である。
> ・これは自社チップ発注の確定材料ではない。
> ・重要なのは、フロンティアAI企業が推論原価と単位エネルギーあたり性能を競争軸に入れた点である。
>
> ■朝刊の確認ポイント
> ・NVIDIAとSKの協力計画は、HBM契約だけで見ない。
> ・wafers、packaging、silicon photonics、韓国供給網まで範囲を確認する。
> ・Samsung HBM4Eは、sample shipmentと量産出荷を分ける。
> ・メモリ不足はメモリ企業の受益である。同時に、クラウドとAIモデル企業の原価圧力である。
> ・AI capexの強さは半導体需要を支える。
> ・ただし、金利、希薄化、株式供給増、proxy premium低下を確認する。
> ・open model、local agent、serving効率化、カスタムシリコンは、需要の場所と利益の取り分を変える。

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKP-NloaIAAjtVX.jpg

### The Data Center Engineer (@DataCenterEngnr)
_Thu Jun 04 18:16:04 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/DataCenterEngnr/status/2062599282004271257)

> Hybrid optoelectronic AI computing architecture claims no active cooling needed. More here: https://t.co/qSWCD7KAEC
>
> Artilux has introduced Inception, a hybrid optoelectronic architecture the company is targeting at next-generation AI computing, with the goal of improving power and area efficiency versus conventional digital electronics.
>
> The company is aiming Inception at AI workloads where scaling pressure shows up as higher energy use, larger chips, heavier data movement, and harder thermal management. Inception combines photonics and electronics in a unified system, built around what Artilux describes as an optoelectronics-enabled hybrid systolic array architecture that is compatible with existing CPU, GPU, TPU, and LPU systems. Artilux says the architecture is intended to run large-scale general matrix–matrix multiplication (GEMM) with no data skew and negligible propagation delay.

### 戲水渔 (@kirkpaper)
_Thu Jun 04 18:28:25 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/kirkpaper/status/2062602389652181455)

> 是否要增持AAOI,可以利用短期内，市场对 AAOI 的定价逻辑非常纯粹：你交得出多少货，我就给你多少估值。
> 1. 盯紧月度/季度产能释放节奏
>  AAOI 在 2026 年底前要实现月产能从 10 万个到 65.5 万个的几何级跨越。
>  短期内必须重点关注其休斯顿等厂区的设备到位率、良品率（Yield Rate）以及招工进度**。如果 800G 的出货量能在二季度和三季度环比连续翻倍，股价将在右侧获得最强的基本面支撑。
> 2. 验证扭亏为盈（Turnaround）的成色
>  Q2 净利润是否顺利转正（EPS 跨过 0 美元生死线），以及毛利是否因为 800G 占比提升而显著拉高。
>  只要 Q2 财报确认公司告别微亏，主流机构资金（Long-only 基金）就会开始将该股纳入常规配置池，带来一波估值中枢的系统性抬升。
> 3. 利用杠杆工具捕获短期动量
>  * 鉴于当前处于 2026 Computex 催化剂的右侧爆发期，AAOG、AAOX、LNOK 这类 2 倍做多工具在短期内的动量（Momentum）极强，非常适合用来捕捉这波由短期产能预期引爆的暴力反弹。
> 🔭 远期前瞻布局：1.6T 切换与硅光子生态（2026 年底 - 2027 年）
> 当短期的业绩兑现后，股价要打开进一步的空间，就必须依赖远期叙事（Narrative）的接力。这时候，我们需要把目光从 AAOI 单个公司，放大到图中的 **EUV（半导体光子学 ETF）** 这一生态链上。
> ```
> 【远期技术演进路径】
>  800G 可插拔光模块 (当前主力) 
>        └───> 1.6T 高速率切换 (2026年底爆发)
>                  └───> 硅光子 & CPO 架构 (未来的终极形态)
>
> 1. 1.6T 时代的先发卡位战
>  * 随着下一代 AI 集群架构在 2026 年底逐步揭幕，**1.6T 光模块将正式进入样品测试和前期导入阶段**。
>  * 远期我们需要验证 AAOI 的**高功率窄线宽泵浦激光器**能否顺利导入头部大客户。谁能率先在 1.6T 规模量产上卡位，谁就能拿走下一阶段最肥美的利润。
> 2. 硅光子与 CPO（共同封装光学）的临界点
>  * 随着传输速率迈向 1.6T 甚至更高，传统的可插拔光模块将遭遇功耗和散热的物理瓶颈。**硅光子技术（Silicon Photonics）将从“备选项”变为“必选项”**。
>  * 远期布局需要紧盯 **EUV ETF** 中那些掌握核心光芯片设计、激光器制造以及先进封装（如 TSMC 的 COWAS 衍生技术）的底层硬科技公司。这是行业规模从百亿级向千亿级跃迁的核心引擎。
> 策略执行落地建议
> | 阶段 | 核心交易工具 | 核心盯盘信号 | 风险防控 |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | **短期（当前 - Q3）** | AAOI、AAOG、AAOX | 季报 EPS 转正、800G 月产能爬坡斜率 | 警惕大客户季度订单回调、杠杆损耗 |
> | **远期（2026年底 - 2027）** | EUV ETF、AAOI（长线底仓） | 1.6T 样品通过率、硅光子产业链标准化进度 | 技术路径切换失败、行业竞争加剧 |
> 在这种“短看产能、远看技术”的框架下，短期冲锋用高弹性的个股或杠杆 ETF 咬住动量，远期用主题型 ETF（如 EUV）去包容技术路径的不确定性，是攻守兼备的最佳配置方式。

### New Hampshire BEA (@NHEconomy)
_Thu Jun 04 18:31:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/NHEconomy/status/2062603229498646747)

> New Hampshire is showcasing its emerging photonics sector at @PhotonicsNorth in Quebec City. Photonics and stochastic silicon are both interesting candidates, but I also expect the singularity to be surprising.

### Ch🅰️rtradamus 🔋 (@Chartradamus)
_Thu Jun 04 19:46:07 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 35 · ↻ 3 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/Chartradamus/status/2062621942885331091)

> $CRDO Fundamental Deep Dive 🟢 Credo Tech
>
> OVERVIEW
>
> Credo operates as a hyper-growth high-speed connectivity semiconductor provider that has a broad portfolio of products spanning SerDes, optical DSPs, Active Electrical Cables (AECs), and silicon photonics solutions. FY2025 proved their explosive growth narrative, achieving an annual revenue of $1.34B, growing +206% YoY. The AI/HPC data center segment delivered the bulk of growth, driven by hyperscaler demand, AI cluster infrastructure, and optical/electrical interconnects (800G/1.6T).
>
> $CRDO is the dominant force in delivering copper architecture through its market-leading AECs. Low-power, high-reliability copper cables that facilitate short-reach intra-rack and spine connections in AI clusters today. Over the coming years, the industry will transition toward photonics for longer-reach, higher-density interconnects at 1.6T+ speeds, where copper hits physical limits. The fear with this development was that Credo would be essentially phased out of the market with time, leading to the massive correction in early 2026.
>
> However, the recent DustPhotonics acquisition (completed in May 2026) brings in-house silicon photonics PIC technology for 800G/1.6T/3.2T+ NPO and CPO, solidifying its future fully vertically integrated stack (SerDes + DSP + silicon photonics + system integration). This positions Credo perfectly for the next decade of AI infrastructure evolution, capturing copper today and optics tomorrow.
>
> In my eyes, This company is a premier "picks-and-shovels" play on the connectivity buildout. Margins are disgustingly high (60%+ gross) now and in the years moving forward with a strong FCF + balance sheet, providing the company a leg-up on competition due to minimal capital intensity given their fabless model. These margins are expected to be sustained or even expand further as higher-ASP optical and silicon photonics products ramp.
>
> --------------------------
>
> GROWTH OUTLOOK
>
> $CRDO has consistently outperformed expectations without sandbagging guidance. Management projects robust revenue growth over the next 3–5 years, driven largely by AI connectivity + photonics acceleration.
>
> Credo maintains deep partnerships with all major hyperscalers (including $MSFT, $AMZN, $META, $ORCL and xAI), a fact known due to their famous "purple cables" acting as visual proof across imaged AI/HPC builds. Their solutions are currently powering xAI’s Colossus cluster via ZeroFlap AECs to maximize GPU utilization and cluster uptime. This is the part many sleep on! These existing relationships give Credo massive leverage to drive future growth when hyperscalers are primed to adopt the new 1.6T+ optical DSPs and silicon photonics products as the transition accelerates.
>
> The AI connectivity segment projects strong growth of ~80%+ YoY in FY26 (with a re-inflection in this strength in the back half of 2027) due to expanded hyperscaler/AI focus. Over FY2026, the company is projected to report ~$2.4B Revenue and ~$6 EPS. I positioned before this inflection starts in March. I am thankful for the opportunity we were provided.
>
> This growth fuels income statement expansion, with non-GAAP gross margins holding steady in the mid-to-high 60s% and operating margins nearing 45-50% as higher-margin optical and photonics products enter the mix further down the line, driving EPS sharply higher. The balance sheet is pristine, currently holding $1.4B in cash with strong FCF generation and zero debt thanks to the fabless model. Product roadmaps support their ambitious outlook, as shown by their unveiling of 1.6T optical DSPs and silicon photonics integration becoming available with next-generation AI programs such as 800G acceleration ramping in 2H 2026. 
>
> --------------------------
>
> FAIR VALUATION ESTIMATE
>
> Using an aggregated/blended valuation approach based on many different disciplines of FA (DCF, Relative Multiples, Analyst Coverage, etcetera)...
>
> FVE = $260/share
>
> This does not take into account the potential for technical momentum to accelerate price far beyond this FVE due to future prospects. One of my favorite tidbits from an FA standpoint for this company is that their NTM P/E is 36.7 and PEG sits at 0.2. This is EXTREMELY LOW in my opinion for the growth promised. Tons of room higher from a valuation standpoint relative to other companies.
>
> --------------------------
>
> LONG-TERM ESTIMATES
>
> Assuming $CRDO meets aggressive growth targets and achieves success in mixing CPO + NPO products into their portfolio with clear customer adoption, this is their potential path forward valuation-wise when using P/E multiples and expected EPS values.
>
> EY2026 = $350+
> EY2027 = $500+
> EY2028 = $700+
> EY2029 = $900+
>
> One of my favorite longs at this time. There is risk involved regarding the integration of DustPhotonics post-acquisition, but I very much so trust management considering their track record.
>
> Credit to @damnang2 for the image breaking down their product portfolio.

### TheValueist (@TheValueist)
_Thu Jun 04 20:11:55 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 40 · ↻ 6 · 💬 7 · [open on X](https://x.com/TheValueist/status/2062628436460413020)

> $MRVL Marvell Technology: Architect of the AI Connectivity Backbone. Investment Thesis.
>
> Marvell Technology has completed a strategic transformation that few legacy semiconductor companies execute cleanly. The pivot away from traditional networking and storage semiconductors toward custom silicon and high-speed connectivity for AI data center infrastructure is not a repositioning in progress — it's largely done, and the financial trajectory is beginning to reflect it. The Celestial AI acquisition extends that positioning into optical interconnects and photonic fabrics, addressing the next layer of AI infrastructure bottleneck where copper interconnects hit physical limits at scale.
>
> The hyperscaler demand dynamic is the engine behind the revenue ramp thesis. Custom ASIC design wins with major cloud providers represent a different category of customer relationship than merchant silicon sales — they create deep technical integration, long program lifecycles, and switching costs that are measured in years of co-development rather than procurement cycles. That stickiness is a genuine competitive moat, but it also concentrates revenue in ways that make the business sensitive to program-level decisions at a small number of accounts.
>
> Matthew Murphy's leadership has been the consistent thread through the transformation. The strategic decisions — which legacy businesses to exit, which adjacencies to pursue, which acquisitions to make — reflect a coherent vision that has been executed with unusual discipline for a company managing simultaneous portfolio transitions. That track record matters when evaluating whether the optical interconnect bet will be executed with similar precision.
>
> Technical execution at advanced nodes is the capability risk that the strategic narrative doesn't eliminate. Custom silicon at leading-edge process nodes requires sustained investment in design talent, EDA infrastructure, and customer co-development resources. The competitive environment for that talent — against hyperscalers building internal silicon teams and peers targeting the same design win opportunities — is intensifying, which adds cost pressure alongside the execution complexity.
>
> The valuation is the honest tension in the thesis. Marvell is priced as a confirmed AI infrastructure compounder, and the revenue ramp forecasts embedded in the current multiple require hyperscaler demand to remain elevated, program ramps to execute on schedule, and optical interconnect adoption to accelerate at the pace the Celestial AI acquisition assumes. Each of those is plausible individually — together, they represent a high bar that leaves the stock exposed to any single point of execution friction. The strategic positioning is among the strongest in the AI semiconductor supply chain; the question is how much of that quality is already in the price.

### ANDREW AARON SKYZ 🐳🌟 (@AndrewAaronSkyy)
_Thu Jun 04 20:12:24 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/AndrewAaronSkyy/status/2062628558019924042)

> The recent buzz surrounding Marvell Technology $MRVL becoming a potential trillion-dollar company stems largely from a high-profile endorsement by Nvidia CEO Jensen Huang at the Computex 2026 trade show. The analysts and industry observers point to several fundamental pillars that support this ambitious valuation thesis:
> 1 Essential Data Center Connectivity: As AI workloads become disaggregated and distributed across thousands of chips, connectivity has become the primary bottleneck. Marvell provides the essential networking and connectivity chips that allow these massive clusters to communicate at the high speeds required for modern AI.  
>
> 2 Strategic Nvidia Partnership: Nvidia, which has a deep interest in the success of the AI ecosystem, recently invested $2 billion in $MRVL. This partnership, centered on NVLink Fusion, aims to integrate their technologies to build more efficient AI infrastructure, essentially making Marvell a critical partner rather than just a vendor.  
>
> 3 Leadership in Custom Silicon (ASICs): Marvell is a leader in custom-designed chips for major hyperscalers like Amazon and Microsoft. Unlike general-purpose GPUs, these ASICs are tailored for specific tasks, creating sticky, multi-year revenue streams that provide a massive, predictable growth foundation.  
>
> 4 Optical Networking Expertise: Marvell is at the forefront of the shift toward optical interconnects, which use light instead of electricity to move data. This technology is critical for scaling AI performance as bandwidth demands continue to explode.  
>
> 5 Industry-Leading Product Innovation: The company recently launched the Teralynx T100, an industry-first 102.4 Tbps switch designed specifically to address latency and energy constraints in AI data centers, keeping them ahead of competitors.  
>
> 6 Rapidly Expanding AI Infrastructure Revenue: Data center operations now drive roughly 74% of Marvell's total revenue. The company has projected strong, sustained double-digit growth in this segment, fueled by the global buildout of AI data centers.  
>
> 7 Aggressive M&A Strategy: Marvell has been strategically acquiring startups like Celestial AI and XConn to bolster its capabilities in advanced packaging and optical interconnects, allowing it to quickly fill gaps in its technological roadmap.  
>
> 8 Silicon Photonics Potential: Marvell is heavily investing in silicon photonics, a technology that promises to significantly improve the energy efficiency and data transfer speeds of future AI clusters. This is widely considered a "real" long-term growth driver.
>
> 9 One-Stop Shop Positioning: By offering a comprehensive suite of solutions, from processors and ASICs to optical I/O and switching. Marvell is positioning itself as a vital, end-to-end infrastructure provider for the cloud-scale AI era.  
>
> 10 Market Momentum and Valuation Re-rating: Following Jensen Huang's endorsement, the market has begun to aggressively re-price Marvell, reflecting the expectation that it will capture a massive share of the AI hardware market in the coming years. This investor confidence acts as a catalyst for the capital influx needed to support a larger market cap.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/tweet_video_thumb/HJ_tvUCWQAA0JM-.jpg

### SynapseX (@TheSynapseX)
_Thu Jun 04 21:20:32 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 2 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/TheSynapseX/status/2062645703940403375)

> 🚨 Scientists shrank a powerful femtosecond laser onto a chip.
>
> This is not a laser pointer upgrade. It is a photonics platform breakthrough.
>
> Ultrafast lasers produce extremely short pulses of light, often used for precision measurement, spectroscopy, medical imaging, atomic clocks, and chemical analysis.
>
> The problem:
>
> Traditional ultrafast laser systems can be bulky and complex.
>
> In a Nature paper, researchers demonstrated an integrated mode-locked laser using an erbium-implanted silicon nitride photonic chip and a Mamyshev oscillator design.
>
> The key result:
> The chip-scale laser produced nanojoule-level pulses, could be compressed to 147 femtoseconds, and directly drove a broad supercontinuum without extra amplification.
>
> Why it matters:
> This could help move powerful ultrafast laser tools from large lab systems toward compact, portable devices.
>
> Important nuance:
> Not a consumer product yet.
> Not replacing every laser system tomorrow.
>
> Still advanced photonics research.
>
> Translation:
> Real chip-scale laser milestone. Smaller tools.
> Big potential for sensing, spectroscopy, medical diagnostics, and precision timing.
>
> Source:
> High-pulse-energy integrated mode-locked laser using a Mamyshev oscillator. Nature. 2026.
> https://t.co/TE9fxK75U4
>
> Follow @TheSynapseX for anti-hype, source-based science and technology corrections.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HJ_9FAkXQAA96OL.jpg

### Joe Williams (@joewilliams)
_Thu Jun 04 21:41:34 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/joewilliams/status/2062650997277954293)

> I've been looking into ZBLAN optical fiber as it's one of the clearer cases for manufacturing in space. 
>
> ZBLAN is a heavy metal fluoride glass fiber. It offers the potential for lower optical loss than conventional silica fiber and transmits across a broader wavelength range into the mid-infrared. These traits could support longer transmission distances and new uses in sensing and communications.
>
> On Earth, producing high-quality ZBLAN has been difficult. Gravity induces convection in the molten glass during the drawing process leads to microscopic crystals and defects that scatter light and limit performance.
>
> In microgravity, these issues are reduced. The glass stays more homogeneous during drawing. Recent work by Flawless Photonics on the International Space Station produced over 11 kilometers of fiber in about a month.
>
> The returned samples are under analysis, and microscope comparisons show much cleaner microstructures than Earth-produced fiber.
>
> Challenges remain. ZBLAN is more brittle than silica and has a larger minimum bend radius, which affects handling. The technology is still in the demonstration phase but commercial production is being planned,and the plan is to manufacture it in space.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKACIN4XwAE7O6c.jpg

### InvestmentGuru (@InvestmentGuru_)

> What a day. The market started red, but the bulls took control as the session progressed. Cooling oil prices and lower bond yields provided relief, helping risk assets recover.
> That said, this is still not a broad participation rally. The market remains highly selective, with money flowing into specific themes rather than lifting everything higher.
> The strategy remains the same: buy the dip in sectors showing relative strength and strong fundamentals. Chasing extended names rarely ends well, but accumulating quality names during pullbacks can provide the best risk/reward.
> Right now, AI infrastructure, photonics, semiconductors, energy, and select space names continue to attract capital. Selective bullish markets reward discipline, not diversification into everything.

### 투자/주식의 생활화 퇴직 오과장 (@datastaion)
_Tue Jun 02 21:14:35 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 7 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/datastaion/status/2061919430054117501)

> 마벨(Marvell) CEO, "구리의 벽(Copper Wall)이 랙 내부로 이동하고 있으며, 이를 해결할 유일한 방법은 공동 패키징 광학(CPO)뿐"이라고 밝혀
>
> *마벨 테크놀로지(Marvell Technology)의 CEO 맷 머피(Matt Murphy)는 "AI 인프라의 다음 주요 병목 현상은 연산(Compute)이나 메모리가 아니라, 바로 연결성(Connectivity)
>
> *머피 CEO는 구리(Copper)에서 광학(Optical) 인터커넥트로의 전환이 먼 미래가 아닌 '지금 당장' 일어나고 있으며, 이는 반도체 산업 역사상 전례가 없을 정도로 거대한 수요의 물결을 일으킬 것이라고 말했음.
>
> *구리의 벽(Copper Wall)의 물리학
>
> - 신호가 구리 케이블을 통해 이동할 수 있는 거리는 대역폭에 반비례
>
> - 레인당 100Gbps 수준: 구리 케이블은 약 5미터까지 도달할 수 있어 하나의 랙(Rack) 내부에서 서버들을 연결하기에 충분.
>
> - ​레인당 200Gbps 수준: 그 거리는 약 2.5미터로 줄어들며, 이는 랙의 높이와 내부 라우팅 요구 사항을 감안할 때 딱 한계치에 해당.
>
> - ​레인당 400Gbps 수준: 현재 업계가 나아가고 있는 이 단계에서는 구리선으로 랙 내부를 완전히 연결하는 것이 더 이상 불가능.
>
> *구리의 벽이 한 단계 이동할 때마다, 광학으로 전환해야 하는 연결의 수는 최소 10배 이상 증가. 머피 CEO는 이를 광학 산업의 '수요 폭발'로 묘사.
>
> *​공동 패키징 광학(CPO): 왜 필요한가?
>
> - 랙 내부에서의 전환은 랙과 랙 사이(Inter-rack)에 사용되는 기존의 광학 기술로는 해결할 수 없다. 랙 내부의 연결 수는 랙 간 연결 수보다 약 10배 더 많음. 이 정도의 밀도에서 표준 광학 모듈을 장착하는 것은 전력과 공간 부족으로 인해 물리적으로 불가능.
>
> - ​CPO는 광 엔진(Optical Engines)을 스위치나 연산 패키지에 직접 통합함으로써 이 문제를 해결. 광섬유를 전면 패널이 아닌 칩(Chip)으로 직접 가져오는 방식. 이 기술은 최첨단 CMOS 공정, 실리콘 포토닉스(SiPh), 첨단 패키징, 그리고 광 인터커넥트를 하나의 긴밀하게 통합된 시스템으로 결합.
>
> - 엔비디아(Nvidia)의 베라 루빈(Vera Rubin) 플랫폼이 이미 생산 단계의 첫 CPO 기반 스위치인 '스펙트럼-X 이더넷 포토닉스(Spectrum-X Ethernet Photonics)'를 도입했다는 점을 언급하며, 이러한 전환이 더 이상 이론에 머물지 않는다는 증거로 제시.
>
> *오늘날의 AI 서버는 구리를 통한 고대역폭 통신을 위해 모든 부품이 서로 가까이 위치해야 하므로 CPU, GPU, 맞춤형 가속기, 메모리, 네트워크 인터페이스가 고정된 구성으로 묶여 있음. 이로 인해 연산 장치 대 메모리의 비율이 배포 시점에 고정되어, 어떤 작업(Workload)이 주어지든 시스템의 일부 자원은 항상 유휴 상태(Underutilized)로 남게 됨.
>
> *​그러나 서버 내부의 연결이 광학으로 바뀌면 거리가 더 이상 아키처를 제약하지 않음. 연산, 메모리, 네트워킹을 각각 독립된 풀(Pool)로 분리(Disaggregated)한 뒤, 각 작업이 실제로 필요로 하는 바에 따라 동적으로 구성(Composed)할 수 있게 됨.
>
> *머피 CEO는 "사상 처음으로 설계자들은 인터커넥트(연결)의 한계가 아니라, 오직 모델의 필요에 맞춰 AI 시스템을 설계할 수 있게 될 것입니다"라고 강조.
>
> https://t.co/VkQZnIMKUB

### Andiamo (@andiamonow)
_Tue Jun 02 21:41:41 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 113 · ↻ 10 · 💬 10 · [open on X](https://x.com/andiamonow/status/2061926249573081367)

> Let me explain what the GlobalFoundries deal actually does for $SIVE — because most retail is reading "partnership" and missing the structural significance.
>
> Reference designs are how foundry ecosystems work.
> When a chip designer wants to build silicon photonics (let's say AMD, Broadcom, or a hyperscaler ASIC team), they don't start from scratch. They start with the foundry's reference design — a pre-validated blueprint for how the components fit together.
> GlobalFoundries' silicon photonics platform is one of the most strategically positioned in the industry. Their SCALE™ optical engine is the foundation for next-generation co-packaged optics.
>
> $SIVE's lasers are now embedded in that reference design.
>
> What this means in practice:
>
> → Every customer who designs silicon photonics on GF's platform starts with $SIVE lasers as the default light source
> → Switching to a non-$SIVE laser requires custom engineering work, custom validation, and supply chain risk
> → $SIVE has effectively become the path of least resistance for the entire GF silicon photonics customer base
>
> The math of why this is different from a normal customer win:
> A typical customer deal = one company buys $SIVE lasers.
>
> A foundry reference design = every customer using that foundry's silicon photonics platform encounters $SIVE lasers in their default design flow.
>
> One captures one customer. The other captures an ecosystem.
>
> The competitive context:
> Coherent, Lumentum, MACOM — these are the larger optical/photonics names retail compares $SIVE to. None of them just got embedded in a major foundry's silicon photonics reference design at the laser layer.
>
> $SIVE just did something its bigger competitors did not.
> And the addressable market GF is targeting? $25B in pluggable optics by 2030.
>
> This is the moat people argued $SIVE didn't have. It just got built. $SIVE

> P.S:  2015 – 2023 Dr. Bastani worked for GlobalFoundries as the Senior VP & GM, Mobile & Wireless Infrastructure; later Senior Advisor to the CEO of GF

> That is $IREN to me.

>

>
