### Wind Info (@WindInfoUS)
_Tue Jun 02 23:47:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 7 · ↻ 2 · 💬 4 · [open on X](https://x.com/WindInfoUS/status/2061957791250776371)

> Wind Financial Morning Post: June 3, 2026
>
> Market Brief
>
> The State Council issues the "15th Five-Year Plan for Accelerating Agricultural and Rural Modernization"
>
> China achieves significant breakthrough in optical communication technology
>
> Shanghai establishes a new landmark for the global asset management center: scale to reach RMB 5.5 trillion by 2030
>
> Prospects for U.S.-Iran negotiations remain uncertain, while applications for transit permits through the Strait of Hormuz have opened
>
> The United States lowers import tariffs on selected steel, aluminum, and copper products, and plans to impose a new 25% tariff on Brazil
>
> Global stock markets rose Tuesday, with U.S. markets hitting new highs and South Korea’s market entering the world’s top six largest securities markets
>
> Tiger Brokers: Suspends new position opening and additional positioning for existing investor accounts in all domestic Chinese instruments effective June 12
>
> Microsoft releases seven new AI models to create an integrated “thinking + programming” agent ecosystem
>
> Top Stories
>
> Shanghai has unveiled 21 measures to deepen its construction as a global asset management center, aiming for total asset management scale of 5.4 trillion yuan by 2030, accounting for one-third of the national total. The city will support listings and mergers of technology firms with strong innovation profiles; accelerate the launch of LNG futures and options; prepare for power and computing power futures; promote the listing of Star 50 Index, Shenzhen 100 Index, ChiNext Index futures and options, and government bond options; enhance mechanisms such as “Shanghai-Hong Kong Stock Connect,” “China-Europe Connect,” and “Bond Connect”; and steadily expand institutional openness in the gold market.
>
> Tiger Brokers announced that, to comply with regulatory requirements during the cross-border securities business consolidation period, it will adjust services for existing investor accounts in mainland China starting June 12. Measures include suspending new positions and additional purchases across all securities products, permitting only sell and close-out transactions; and halting inbound fund transfers while maintaining outbound transfer functionality. The company reported first-quarter revenue of $155 million, up 26.3% year-over-year, and operating profit of $48 million, up 17.5%.
>
> According to Iranian sources, the system for applying for vessel transit permits through the Strait of Hormuz has been fully opened, allowing global shipowners and captains to submit applications. Upon approval, vessels will receive transit authorization. Iranian media reported that information exchanges between Iran and the U.S. have been suspended for several days, despite Western media and officials claiming ongoing dialogue. U.S. President Trump stated that talks with Iran continue. U.S. Secretary of State Rubio affirmed that negotiations are still underway but expressed uncertainty over a potential agreement.
>
> Microsoft unveiled seven new AI models at the Build 2026 developer conference, covering full-stack capabilities in reasoning, coding, vision, speech, and multimodal functions. Its flagship reasoning model, MAI-Thinking-1, matched Anthropic’s Claude Sonnet 4.6 on coding benchmarks. The 5-billion-parameter coding model, MAI-Code-1-Flash, targets the GitHub ecosystem. Microsoft also introduced Web IQ, a search engine defined as a “network intelligence layer for AI agents.”
>
> China Macro & Policy
>
> The State Council issued the “15th Five-Year Plan for Accelerating Agricultural and Rural Modernization,” outlining major projects including high-standard farmland construction and cold-chain logistics facilities. The plan promotes diversified food development and the “AI+” agriculture initiative, and identifies key policy measures to cultivate emerging and future industries in agriculture.
>
> National Development and Reform Commission (NDRC) Director Zheng Zhijie convened a meeting with state-owned enterprises to discuss deepening SOE reform, advancing the national unified market, promoting green and low-carbon development, and ensuring energy security. Zheng emphasized enhancing the technological innovation, industrial control, and security support functions of state-owned enterprises.
>
> The Ministry of Finance recently allocated 99.9 billion yuan in childcare subsidies for 2026, a 10.6% increase from last year, to support local governments in providing subsidies to eligible infants. Total fiscal subsidies for the year are projected to reach approximately 110 billion yuan.
>
> The People’s Bank of China reported that in May, standing lending facility (SLF) net injections amounted to 900 million yuan, pledged supplementary lending (PSL) net withdrawals totaled 154.5 billion yuan, and other structural monetary policy tools net injected 112.9 billion yuan; open market treasury purchases resulted in a net injection of 50 billion yuan.
>
> China’s first online tax-refund-for-overseas-tourists store has officially launched in Beijing, alongside the simultaneous activation of centralized tax-refund points in the city’s hotel sector. Overseas visitors can now process tax refunds directly at hotels after online purchases, expanding the scope of tax-refund services.
>
> China Equities Markets
>
> A-share markets climbed modestly, with the SSE Index rising 0.43% to 4,075.10, the Shenzhen Component Index up 1.63%, and the ChiNext Index jumping 2.66%. The Wind All China Index gained 0.75%, with total market turnover reaching 2.81 trillion yuan. The AI computing hardware supply chain strengthened again, with CPO and optical fiber sectors surging. Components, AI PCs, PCBs, and MLCC concepts advanced. Coal stocks maintained strength, while film and theater, and short-form video game concepts declined.
>
> The Hang Seng Index closed up 2.52% at 26,038.32, the Hang Seng Tech Index surged 4.72%, and the Hang Seng China Enterprises Index rose 3%. Technology stocks rallied broadly, with Tencent Holdings soaring over 10%. New energy vehicles and non-ferrous metals led gains, while AI applications and coal stocks declined. Net inflows via the Southbound Stock Connect totaled 2.2 billion Hong Kong dollars, with Tencent Holdings experiencing 2.1 billion Hong Kong dollars in net outflows.
>
> Fund managers led by Jin Zicai announced that to ensure stable fund operations and protect investor interests, subscription limits for multiple funds — including Caichong Growth Optimum, Caichong Value Momentum, Caichong Integrated Circuit Industry, and Caichong Quality Selection — have been lowered to 1,000 yuan.
>
> The Shanghai Stock Exchange website shows that Yushu Technology’s STAR Market IPO status has changed to “submitted for registration.” Yushu Technology’s market director Huang Jiawei revealed that the company’s new-generation humanoid robot reference design, H2 Plus, developed jointly with NVIDIA, will launch in the second half of the year.
>
> China Industry News
>
> China has achieved a major breakthrough in optical communications. The world’s first S+C+L triple-band (short, conventional, and long wavelength) ultra-low-loss multi-core optical cable line has been officially commissioned in Qingdao, Shandong. The single-fiber capacity exceeds five times that of traditional fibers, fully meeting future demands for AI computing and terabit-per-second ultra-high-speed transmission.
>
> Four ministries have launched the “Sword Net 2026” campaign to combat online copyright infringement, with a focus on AI-related copyright issues. The initiative targets violations such as “remixing,” “plagiarism,” and deepfake content in large model training datasets.
>
> According to Centaline Property Research, 141,000 second-hand residential units were sold in 20 cities in May, up 19.3% year-over-year, with the growth rate expanding 6.3 percentage points from April. Beijing and Shanghai recorded 16,000 and 28,000 second-hand home sales respectively, up 12.1% and 30.9% year-over-year, marking the highest May levels in nearly five years. The average second-hand home price across 100 cities fell 0.32% month-over-month, while new home prices rose 0.16%.
>
> Guangzhou’s Nansha District unveiled “Ten Measures” for real estate policy, launching an “old-home-for-new-home” initiative where proceeds from selling an old property can be directly applied toward a new purchase. A subsidy of 1% of the new home’s total price — capped at 20,000 yuan per unit — will be provided, and this can be stacked with municipal subsidies.
>
> The China Passenger Car Association estimated that domestic new energy passenger vehicle wholesale sales reached 1.36 million units in May, up over 11% year-over-year and month-over-month. According to the China Automobile Dealers Association, the automobile consumption index stood at 81 in May, slightly higher than April, suggesting a continued steady upward trend in overall sales for June.
>
> Fintech
>
> Shanghai’s guidelines on deepening its global asset management center status encourage asset managers to leverage AI, blockchain, and big data technologies to accelerate intelligent investment research and advisory services. The city will support the establishment of AI application pilot bases for asset management.
>
> The Hong Kong Securities and Futures Commission issued a circular requiring licensed institutions — particularly online brokers and virtual asset platforms — to strengthen cybersecurity measures to counter emerging threats driven by advanced AI models.
>
> Corporate News & Updates
>
> Sources indicate Tencent has completed prototype testing of its WeChat AI agent and will initiate compliance review procedures as early as this month. Users will be able to use the agent to trigger hundreds of mini-programs for daily tasks such as food ordering. The project has been designated the highest strategic priority. Tencent Cloud has reduced pricing for the DeepSeek-V4 series models by up to 97.5%.
>
> NVIDIA CEO Jensen Huang stated that agent-based AI will fundamentally reshape all AI applications and represent the most important computing transformation over the next decade. Huang also said Marvell Technology will become the next trillion-dollar company. NVIDIA announced full-scale mass production of its NVIDIA Spectrum-X Ethernet silicon photonics technology based on CPO.
>
> Samsung Electronics unveiled its eighth-generation high-bandwidth memory chip, HBM5, and publicly introduced its HPB cooling solution for the first time. Chief Technology Officer Jae-Hyung Song confirmed that HPB technology has been validated on HBM4E chips and will be commercially deployed with HBM5.
>
> Intel CEO Pat Gelsinger, in his Computex 2026 keynote, said agentic AI is reshaping computing demand, and future AI infrastructure will enter a heterogeneous era of co-development among CPUs, GPUs, ASICs, and custom chips. Demand for CPUs in data centers is expected to re-enter a growth cycle.
>
> SK Group Chairman Choi Tae-won said the global shortage of memory chips may persist until 2030, and the company is increasing capital expenditures to bridge the supply-demand gap. SK Hynix plans to double its wafer capacity over the next five years.
>
> ByteDance’s DouBao large model is expected to launch paid content in late June, with plans to integrate e-commerce functions in the third quarter to drive traffic to Douyin Mall. Longer-term operational strategies are not ruled out.
>
> Anthropic announced the expansion of its Glasswing initiative to 150 new partner organizations across more than 15 countries. These institutions will use the Mythos tool to identify software vulnerabilities. New partners span energy, water, healthcare, telecommunications, and hardware industries.
>
> OpenAI released a suite of new plugins for its Codex agent, covering public equity investment, banking, and sales use cases, and plans to introduce legal and corporate finance functions soon. OpenAI also intends to integrate Codex into ChatGPT.
>
> Alibaba Cloud’s Qwen model launched Qwen3.7-Plus, a multimodal large model capable of understanding images and videos, performing deep reasoning, self-programming, tool invocation, validation, and autonomous iteration. It can complete complex, long-horizon tasks such as replicating smartphone apps and desktop software with a single command.
>
> Global Macro & Policy
>
> U.S. President Trump signed an executive order temporarily adjusting import tariffs on certain steel, aluminum, and copper products, effective June 8 through December 31, 2027. Import tariffs on harvesters and other agricultural machinery will be reduced from 25% to 15%, and the domestic content threshold for imported steel, aluminum, and copper will be lowered from 95% to 85%.
>
> The United States plans to impose 25% punitive tariffs on a range of Brazilian imports, including electronic payment services, preferential tariff treatment, intellectual property protections, and ethanol market access. Exemptions include beef, coffee, rare earth minerals, aircraft and aircraft parts, crude oil, fertilizers, and numerous fruits and nuts.
>
> The Canadian government has proposed to the U.S. and Mexico that the USMCA be renewed for 16 years to avoid triggering the agreement’s mandatory annual review process. Under USMCA provisions, the three nations are scheduled to conduct their first joint review in July. The agreement, signed in 2018 and effective since July 2020, is set to expire in 2036.
>
> U.S. officials are reportedly discussing whether to deploy nuclear weapons in additional NATO European countries. The U.S. already deploys nuclear-capable bombers in Belgium, Germany, Italy, the Netherlands, Turkey, and the UK, and has signaled openness to additional deployments.
>
> Hawkish voices within the Federal Reserve are intensifying. Cleveland Fed President Harker said while maintaining current rates remains appropriate, persistent inflation data may soon necessitate policy action — including potential further rate hikes — to counter elevated inflation risks.
>
> Labor market resilience continues to bolster Fed hawkish expectations. U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics data showed job openings rose to 7.62 million in April, the highest level in two years and well above the 6.87 million forecast. Layoffs fell to 1.692 million, significantly below expectations.
>
> The European Union plans to impose strict eligibility criteria for cloud computing services in key public procurement projects, potentially excluding Amazon, Microsoft, and Google. The proposal aims to reduce EU dependence on U.S. tech products and promote domestic industry development.
>
> Eurostat preliminary data showed euro area CPI rose 3.2% year-over-year in May, up from 3% in April, reinforcing market expectations of a modest ECB rate hike in June.
>
> South Korea’s central bank is poised to raise rates. Statistics Korea reported that May CPI rose 3.1% year-over-year, the largest increase since March 2024. Core CPI increased 2.5%, the highest since February 2024.
>
> The World Meteorological Organization released a report indicating most climate models predict this El Niño will develop into at least a moderate event and may intensify further. Seasonal forecasts suggest most regions will experience above-average temperatures in the coming months.
>
> Global Equity Markets
>
> U.S. major indices closed slightly higher: the Dow Jones Industrial Average rose 0.45% to 51,307.79, the S&P 500 gained 0.13% to 7,609.78, and the Nasdaq Composite edged up 0.03% to 27,093.90 — all closing at record highs. Cisco rose over 5%, Caterpillar gained more than 5%, leading the Dow. The Wind US Magnificent Seven Index declined 1.05%, with Microsoft down over 4% and Google down nearly 4%. The Nasdaq China Golden Dragon Index rose 1.83%, with Canadian Solar up over 12% and Hesai Group up over 8%. Traders closely monitored developments in U.S.-Iran relations and major tech stock performance.
>
> European indices closed higher: Germany’s DAX rose 0.48% to 25,124.17, France’s CAC 40 gained 0.77% to 8,209.09, and the UK’s FTSE 100 climbed 0.33% to 10,373.51. Progress in ceasefire negotiations between Iran and the U.S. lifted risk appetite, but Brent crude breached $95 per barrel, maintaining upward pressure on inflation expectations.
>
> Asia-Pacific markets closed mixed. South Korea’s KOSPI swung sharply — initially surging before plunging more than 3% — and ultimately closed up 0.15% at 8,801.49, setting a new record. South Korea’s total market capitalization surpassed India’s, becoming the world’s sixth-largest stock market. Japan’s Nikkei 225 fell 0.3% to 66,734.24. India’s SENSEX rose 0.52% to 74,649.84.
>
> Andrew Left, founder of the renowned short-selling firm Citron Research, was convicted by a U.S. court of stock manipulation and may face decades in prison. The case could mark a landmark moment for short-sellers globally and reshape regulatory boundaries for short reports and market commentary.
>
> Data from India’s National Securities Depository Limited showed that as of June 1, foreign institutional investors’ net investment in Indian equities totaled 7.3 trillion rupees — the lowest since 2016. Global fund ownership in Indian equities has declined from nearly 20% a decade ago to 15% today.
>
> Bonds
>
> China’s interbank bond market traded in a narrow range, with yields on major government bonds moving slightly in different directions. Treasury futures rallied slightly at the close, with the 10-year contract up 0.06%. Liquidity conditions returned to ample levels as the PBOC conducted 200 million yuan in reverse repo operations, resulting in a net withdrawal of 248.8 billion yuan.
>
> U.S. Treasury yields were mixed: the 2-year yield rose 1.24 basis points to 4.039%, the 3-year yield rose 0.59 basis points to 4.085%, the 5-year yield held steady at 4.163%, the 10-year yield fell 1.18 basis points to 4.439%, and the 30-year yield declined 1.21 basis points to 4.957%.
>
> Commodities
>
> U.S. crude oil futures rose 1.33% to $93.39 per barrel; Brent crude gained 1.01% to $95.94 per barrel. U.S. API crude inventories fell sharply, exceeding market expectations, while geopolitical tensions in the Middle East — including Iran’s suspension of U.S.-Iran talks and its plan to block the Strait of Hormuz — heightened concerns over supply disruptions. The strait handles roughly 20% of global oil shipments, and global crude inventories remain at low levels, jointly supporting higher prices.
>
> International precious metals futures generally rose: COMEX gold futures gained 0.29% to $4,519.20 per ounce, and COMEX silver futures rose 0.25% to $75.44 per ounce. Geopolitical tensions in the Middle East lifted safe-haven demand, while rising U.S. and European rate expectations weighed on market sentiment, creating a tug-of-war.
>
> Most base metals on the LME rose: LME tin climbed 2.88% to $58,280 per ton, LME lead gained 1.52% to $2,037 per ton, LME zinc rose 1.48% to $3,631 per ton, LME aluminum advanced 1.20% to $3,760.50 per ton, LME copper increased 1.10% to $13,983.50 per ton, while LME nickel edged down 0.19% to $19,215 per ton.
>
> The European Central Bank reported that as of the end of 2025, gold accounted for 27% of global official reserve assets, surpassing U.S. Treasuries, which fell to 22%. Gold has become the world’s largest official reserve asset.
>
> Abu Dhabi National Oil Company (ADNOC) revealed plans to construct a refined products pipeline to bypass the Strait of Hormuz. The company is also exploring a new east-west crude oil trunk line that would allow other Gulf producers to route exports through UAE territory, avoiding the strait.
>
> FX & Currency Markets
>
> Onshore renminbi closed at 6.7622 against the U.S. dollar at 16:30, up 28 basis points from the previous close, and settled at 6.7650 in the night session. The PBOC’s mid-rate was set at 6.8187, a 20-basis-point depreciation from the prior day.
>
> At the close of New York trading, the U.S. Dollar Index rose 0.03% to 99.22. Non-U.S. currencies were mixed: the euro fell 0.01% to 1.1631, the pound rose 0.07% to 1.3464, the Australian dollar rose 0.27% to 0.7180, the dollar rose 0.16% against the yen to 159.9295, the dollar fell 0.01% against the Canadian dollar to 1.3839, the dollar rose 0.08% against the Swiss franc to 0.7873, and the offshore renminbi gained 23 basis points to 6.7629.
>
> Japan’s authorities issued a strong signal after record-sized foreign exchange interventions proved ineffective. Finance Minister Kato said the government stands ready to take appropriate action on exchange rates if necessary.
>

### LIWEI_TW Capital (@LIWEI_TWCapital)
_Tue Jun 02 23:57:23 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 43 · ↻ 2 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/LIWEI_TWCapital/status/2061960400871293007)

> Since $MRVL was up +32%, let me introduce you Taiwan’s Most Direct $MRVL related Stock: LuxNet Corporation 華星光（4979):
>
> Marvell’s push into high-speed Optical DSPs and silicon photonics/CPO solutions for AI data centers has created clear demand for supporting photonic components. LuxNet stands out because of its specific role and long-term relationship with Marvell.
>
> Here’s why the linkage is considered particularly direct:
>
> 1.  Critical Photonic Component Supplier
>
> LuxNet produces InP-based CW Lasers, which serve as the essential external light source in silicon photonics and CPO architectures. These lasers are a key part of enabling Marvell’s advanced Optical DSP platforms.
>
> 2.  Long-Standing Partnership
> The relationship goes back to Marvell’s acquisition of Inphi. 
>
> LuxNet has been a manufacturing and development partner for Marvell’s high-speed optical transceiver modules and continues to work with the company on next-generation solutions.
>
> 3.  Frequently Cited in Market Coverage
>
> When Marvell reports progress in optical or silicon photonics, or when Nvidia deepens cooperation with Marvell, LuxNet is regularly included in analyst and media lists of the most direct Taiwan beneficiaries.
>
> Example: Recent coverage on Nvidia-Marvell silicon photonics collaboration highlighted LuxNet as part of the Taiwan optical supply chain that stands to benefit.
> 4.  Higher Specificity Than Most Peers
> Unlike broader semiconductor or foundry plays, LuxNet’s involvement is more component-specific and tied directly to Marvell’s optical product roadmap, making the supply chain connection more visible and targeted.
>
> This combination of technical role, historical partnership, and consistent market recognition is why LuxNet is often viewed as one of the clearest $MRVL supply chain exposures in Taiwan.
>
